title="Metropolitan City of Venice">Metropolitan City of Venice</a>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ca%27Loredan_Venice.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Ca%27Loredan_Venice.jpg/84px-Ca%27Loredan_Venice.jpg" width="84" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Ca%27Loredan_Venice.jpg/126px-Ca%27Loredan_Venice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Ca%27Loredan_Venice.jpg/168px-Ca%27Loredan_Venice.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3520" data-file-height="5034" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><i>Ca\' Loredan</i>, Venice\'s City Hall\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<p>The legislative body of the <a href="/wiki/Comune" title="Comune">municipality</a> is the City Council (<i>Consiglio Comunale</i>), which is composed of 45 councillors elected every five years with a proportional system, contextually<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> to the mayoral elections. The executive body is the City Committee (<i>Giunta Comunale</i>), composed of 12 <a href="/wiki/Assessor_(Italy)" title="Assessor (Italy)">assessors</a> nominated and presided over by a directly elected <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">Mayor</a>.\n</p><p>Venice was governed by center-left parties from the 1990s until the 2010s, when the mayor started to be elected directly. Its region <a href="/wiki/Veneto" title="Veneto">Veneto</a> has long been a conservative stronghold, with the coalition between the regionalist <a href="/wiki/Lega_Nord" title="Lega Nord">Lega Nord</a> and the center-right <a href="/wiki/Forza_Italia_(2013)" title="Forza Italia (2013)">Forza Italia</a> winning absolute majorities of the electorate in many elections at communal, national, and regional levels.\n</p><p>After a corruption scandal that forced the center-left mayor <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Orsoni" title="Giorgio Orsoni">Giorgio Orsoni</a> to resign, Venice voted for the first time in June 2015 for a conservative directly elected mayor: the center-right businessman <a href="/wiki/Luigi_Brugnaro" title="Luigi Brugnaro">Luigi Brugnaro</a> won the election in the second round of voting with the 53% of the votes against the leftist magistrate and member of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Senate" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian Senate">Italian Senate</a> <a href="/wiki/Felice_Casson" title="Felice Casson">Felice Casson</a>, who led in the first round with 38% of the votes.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:La_villa_Bianca_(Lido_de_Venise)_(8150126764).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/La_villa_Bianca_%28Lido_de_Venise%29_%288150126764%29.jpg/220px-La_villa_Bianca_%28Lido_de_Venise%29_%288150126764%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/La_villa_Bianca_%28Lido_de_Venise%29_%288150126764%29.jpg/330px-La_villa_Bianca_%28Lido_de_Venise%29_%288150126764%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/La_villa_Bianca_%28Lido_de_Venise%29_%288150126764%29.jpg/440px-La_villa_Bianca_%28Lido_de_Venise%29_%288150126764%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:La_villa_Bianca_(Lido_de_Venise)_(8150126764).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Villa Bianca in the residential district of <a href="/wiki/Lido_di_Venezia" title="Lido di Venezia">Lido</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The municipality of Venice is subdivided into six administrative Boroughs (<i>Municipalit\xc3\xa0</i>). Each Borough is governed by a Council (<i>Consiglio</i>) and a President, elected contextually<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> to the city Mayor. The urban organization is governed by the Italian Constitution (art. 114). The Boroughs have the power to advise the Mayor with nonbinding opinions on a large spectrum of topics (environment, construction, public health, local markets) and exercise the functions delegated to them by the City Council; in addition they are supplied with autonomous funding to finance local activities. The Boroughs are:\n</p><p><i>Lagoon area:</i>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Venezia (<i>historic city</i>)-<a href="/wiki/Murano" title="Murano">Murano</a>\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/Burano" title="Burano">Burano</a> (also known as <i>Venezia insulare</i>); population: 69,136;</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lido_di_Venezia" title="Lido di Venezia">Lido</a>\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/Pellestrina" title="Pellestrina">Pellestrina</a> (also known as <i>Venezia litorale</i>); population: 21,664.</li></ul>\n<p><i>Mainland (terraferma)</i>, annexed with a Royal Decree, in 1926, to the municipality of Venezia:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Favaro_Veneto" title="Favaro Veneto">Favaro Veneto</a>; population: 23,615;</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mestre" title="Mestre">Mestre</a>-Carpenedo (also known as <i>Mestre centro</i>); population: 88,952;</li>\n<li>Chirignago-Zelarino; population: 38;179;</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Marghera" title="Marghera">Marghera</a>; population: 28;466.</li></ul>\n<p>After the 2015 elections, five of the six boroughs are governed by the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Italy)" title="Democratic Party (Italy)">Democratic Party</a> and its allies, and one by the center-right mayoral majority.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Venice" title="Economic history of Venice">Venice\'s economy</a> has changed throughout history.  Although there is little specific information about the earliest years, it is likely that an important source of the city\'s prosperity was the trade in slaves, captured in central Europe and sold to North Africa and the Levant.  Venice\'s location at the head of the Adriatic, and directly south of the terminus of the Brenner Pass over the Alps, would have given it a distinct advantage as a middleman in this important trade. In the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a>, Venice was a major center for commerce and trade, as it controlled a vast sea-empire, and became an extremely wealthy European city, a leader in political and economic affairs and a centre for trade and commerce.<sup id="cite_ref-aboutvenice.org_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aboutvenice.org-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> From the 11th century until the 15th century, <a href="/wiki/Pilgrimage" title="Pilgrimage">pilgrimages</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Land" title="Holy Land">Holy Land</a> were offered in Venice. Other ports such as <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pisa" title="Pisa">Pisa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Marseille</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancona" title="Ancona">Ancona</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dubrovnik" title="Dubrovnik">Dubrovnik</a> were hardly able to make any competition to the well organized transportation of pilgrims from Venice.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tourism_on_the_Canal_in_Burano_(Venice).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Tourism_on_the_Canal_in_Burano_%28Venice%29.jpg/220px-Tourism_on_the_Canal_in_Burano_%28Venice%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Tourism_on_the_Canal_in_Burano_%28Venice%29.jpg/330px-Tourism_on_the_Canal_in_Burano_%28Venice%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Tourism_on_the_Canal_in_Burano_%28Venice%29.jpg/440px-Tourism_on_the_Canal_in_Burano_%28Venice%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2700" data-file-height="1802" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tourism_on_the_Canal_in_Burano_(Venice).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Like Murano, Burano is also a tourist destination, usually reached via vaporetto</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Praia_de_Veneza_(483008092).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Praia_de_Veneza_%28483008092%29.jpg/220px-Praia_de_Veneza_%28483008092%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Praia_de_Veneza_%28483008092%29.jpg/330px-Praia_de_Veneza_%28483008092%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Praia_de_Veneza_%28483008092%29.jpg/440px-Praia_de_Veneza_%28483008092%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Praia_de_Veneza_(483008092).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The beach of <a href="/wiki/Lido_di_Venezia" title="Lido di Venezia">Lido di Venezia</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wenecja_Most_Westchnie%C5%84.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Wenecja_Most_Westchnie%C5%84.JPG/220px-Wenecja_Most_Westchnie%C5%84.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Wenecja_Most_Westchnie%C5%84.JPG/330px-Wenecja_Most_Westchnie%C5%84.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Wenecja_Most_Westchnie%C5%84.JPG/440px-Wenecja_Most_Westchnie%C5%84.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wenecja_Most_Westchnie%C5%84.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bridge_of_Sighs" title="Bridge of Sighs">Bridge of Sighs</a>, one of the most visited sites in the city</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arsenal_-_panoramio_-_nikola_pu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Arsenal_-_panoramio_-_nikola_pu.jpg/220px-Arsenal_-_panoramio_-_nikola_pu.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Arsenal_-_panoramio_-_nikola_pu.jpg/330px-Arsenal_-_panoramio_-_nikola_pu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Arsenal_-_panoramio_-_nikola_pu.jpg/440px-Arsenal_-_panoramio_-_nikola_pu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arsenal_-_panoramio_-_nikola_pu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Venetian_Arsenal" title="Venetian Arsenal">Venetian Arsenal</a> houses the <a href="/wiki/Museo_Storico_Navale" title="Museo Storico Navale">Naval Historical Museum</a></div></div></div>\n<p>This all changed by the 17th century, when Venice\'s trade empire was taken over by other countries such as Portugal, and its naval importance was reduced. In the 18th century, then, it became a major agricultural and industrial exporter. The 18th century\'s biggest industrial complex was the <a href="/wiki/Venice_Arsenal" class="mw-redirect" title="Venice Arsenal">Venice Arsenal</a>, and the Italian Army still uses it today (even though some space has been used for major theatrical and cultural productions, and spaces for art).<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Since World War II many Venetians have moved to Mestre and Marghera seeking employment as well as affordable housing.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Today, Venice\'s economy is mainly based on tourism, shipbuilding (mainly done in the neighboring cities of <a href="/wiki/Mestre" title="Mestre">Mestre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Porto_Marghera" class="mw-redirect" title="Porto Marghera">Porto Marghera</a>), services, trade and industrial exports.<sup id="cite_ref-aboutvenice.org_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aboutvenice.org-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Murano_glass" title="Murano glass">Murano glass</a> production in <a href="/wiki/Murano" title="Murano">Murano</a> and lace production in <a href="/wiki/Burano" title="Burano">Burano</a> are also highly important to the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-aboutvenice.org_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aboutvenice.org-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city is facing financial challenges. In late 2016, it had a major deficit in its budget and debts in excess of  \xe2\x82\xac400 million. "In effect, the place is bankrupt", according to a report by <a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-theguardian.com_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theguardian.com-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Many locals are leaving the historic center due to rapidly increasing rental costs. The declining native population affects the character of the city as an October 2016 <a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Geographic (magazine)">National Geographic</a> article pointed out in its subtitle: "Residents are abandoning the city, which is in danger of becoming an overpriced theme park".<sup id="cite_ref-news.nationalgeographic.com_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news.nationalgeographic.com-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2017, Italy was required to bail out two banks in Venice to prevent bankruptcies of the <a href="/wiki/Banca_Popolare_di_Vicenza" title="Banca Popolare di Vicenza">Banca Popolare di Vicenza</a> and <a href="/wiki/Veneto_Banca" title="Veneto Banca">Veneto Banca</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Both companies will be wound down and their assets with value will be taken over by another Italian bank, Intesa Sanpaolo which received \xe2\x82\xac5.2 billion as compensation. The Italian government will be responsible for losses from any uncollectible loans from the now closed banks. The cost may be as high as \xe2\x82\xac5.2 billion but the guarantees to cover bad loans total \xe2\x82\xac12 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Venice_Piazza_San_Marco,_Doge%27s_Palace.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Venice_Piazza_San_Marco%2C_Doge%27s_Palace.jpg/220px-Venice_Piazza_San_Marco%2C_Doge%27s_Palace.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Venice_Piazza_San_Marco%2C_Doge%27s_Palace.jpg/330px-Venice_Piazza_San_Marco%2C_Doge%27s_Palace.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Venice_Piazza_San_Marco%2C_Doge%27s_Palace.jpg/440px-Venice_Piazza_San_Marco%2C_Doge%27s_Palace.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Venice_Piazza_San_Marco,_Doge%27s_Palace.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Piazza_San_Marco" title="Piazza San Marco">Piazza San Marco</a>. <a href="/wiki/Doge%27s_Palace" title="Doge&#39;s Palace">Doge\'s Palace</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gondola_on_the_Grand_Canal,_Venice,_Italy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Gondola_on_the_Grand_Canal%2C_Venice%2C_Italy.jpg/220px-Gondola_on_the_Grand_Canal%2C_Venice%2C_Italy.jpg" width="220" height="101" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Gondola_on_the_Grand_Canal%2C_Venice%2C_Italy.jpg/330px-Gondola_on_the_Grand_Canal%2C_Venice%2C_Italy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Gondola_on_the_Grand_Canal%2C_Venice%2C_Italy.jpg/440px-Gondola_on_the_Grand_Canal%2C_Venice%2C_Italy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3300" data-file-height="1512" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gondola_on_the_Grand_Canal,_Venice,_Italy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gondolas share the waterway with other types of craft (including the vaporetti)</div></div></div>\n<p>Venice is an important tourist destination for its celebrated art and architecture.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The city gets up to 60,000 tourists per day (2017 estimate). Estimates as to the annual number of tourists vary from 22 million to 30 million.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph.co.uk_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph.co.uk-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-independent.co.uk_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent.co.uk-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> This \'<a href="/wiki/Overtourism" class="mw-redirect" title="Overtourism">overtourism</a>\' creates overcrowding and <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_tourism" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental impact of tourism">environmental problems</a> in its canal ecosystem. By 2017, <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> was considering the addition of Venice to its "In-Danger" list which includes historical ruins in war-torn countries. To reduce the number of visitors that are causing irreversible changes in Venice, the agency supports limiting the number of cruise ships<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> as well as creating a full strategy for a more sustainable tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cruiseship_passing_bacino_San_Marco_Venise.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Cruiseship_passing_bacino_San_Marco_Venise.jpg/220px-Cruiseship_passing_bacino_San_Marco_Venise.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Cruiseship_passing_bacino_San_Marco_Venise.jpg/330px-Cruiseship_passing_bacino_San_Marco_Venise.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Cruiseship_passing_bacino_San_Marco_Venise.jpg/440px-Cruiseship_passing_bacino_San_Marco_Venise.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6504" data-file-height="4344" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cruiseship_passing_bacino_San_Marco_Venise.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cruise ship passing bacino San Marco</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2017_06_Venezia_Terminal_Passeggeri_-_Giudecca_Canal_2629.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/2017_06_Venezia_Terminal_Passeggeri_-_Giudecca_Canal_2629.jpg/220px-2017_06_Venezia_Terminal_Passeggeri_-_Giudecca_Canal_2629.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/2017_06_Venezia_Terminal_Passeggeri_-_Giudecca_Canal_2629.jpg/330px-2017_06_Venezia_Terminal_Passeggeri_-_Giudecca_Canal_2629.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/2017_06_Venezia_Terminal_Passeggeri_-_Giudecca_Canal_2629.jpg/440px-2017_06_Venezia_Terminal_Passeggeri_-_Giudecca_Canal_2629.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2001" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2017_06_Venezia_Terminal_Passeggeri_-_Giudecca_Canal_2629.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">Cruise ships</a> access the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Venice" title="Port of Venice">port of Venice</a> through the <a href="/wiki/Giudecca_Canal" title="Giudecca Canal">Giudecca Canal</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Tourism has been a major sector of Venetian industry since the 18th century, when it was a major center for the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Tour" title="Grand Tour">Grand Tour</a>, with its beautiful cityscape, uniqueness, and rich musical and artistic cultural heritage. In the 19th century, it became a fashionable centre for the "rich and famous", often staying or dining at luxury establishments such as the Danieli Hotel and the <a href="/wiki/Caff%C3%A8_Florian" title="Caff\xc3\xa8 Florian">Caff\xc3\xa8 Florian</a>. It continued being a fashionable city in vogue right into the early 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> In the 1980s, the <a href="/wiki/Carnival_of_Venice" title="Carnival of Venice">Carnival of Venice</a> was revived and the city has become a major centre of international conferences and festivals, such as the prestigious <a href="/wiki/Venice_Biennale" title="Venice Biennale">Venice Biennale</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Venice_Film_Festival" title="Venice Film Festival">Venice Film Festival</a>, which attract visitors from all over the world for their theatrical, cultural, cinematic, artistic, and musical productions.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Today, there are numerous attractions in Venice, such as <a href="/wiki/St_Mark%27s_Basilica" title="St Mark&#39;s Basilica">St Mark\'s Basilica</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Doge%27s_Palace" title="Doge&#39;s Palace">Doge\'s Palace</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Canal_(Venice)" title="Grand Canal (Venice)">Grand Canal</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Piazza_San_Marco" title="Piazza San Marco">Piazza San Marco</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Lido_di_Venezia" title="Lido di Venezia">Lido di Venezia</a> is also a popular international luxury destination, attracting thousands of actors, critics, celebrities, and mainly people in the cinematic industry. The city also relies heavily on the cruise business.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_62-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The Cruise Venice Committee has estimated that cruise ship passengers spend more than 150 million euros (US $193 million) annually in the city according to a 2015 report.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Other reports, however, point out that such day trippers spend relatively little in the few hours of their visits to the city.<sup id="cite_ref-theguardian.com_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theguardian.com-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Venice is regarded by some as a tourist trap, and by others as a "living museum".<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_62-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>  Unlike most other places in Western Europe, and the world, Venice has become widely known for its element of <a href="/wiki/Elegant_decay" title="Elegant decay">elegant decay</a>. The competition for foreigners to buy homes in Venice has made prices rise so high that numerous inhabitants are forced to move to more affordable areas of <a href="/wiki/Veneto" title="Veneto">Veneto</a> and Italy, the most notable being <a href="/wiki/Mestre" title="Mestre">Mestre</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Minimising_the_effects_of_tourism">Minimising the effects of tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Minimising the effects of tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The need to balance the jobs produced by cruise tourism with the protection of the city\'s historic environment and fragile canals has seen the Italian Transport Ministry attempt to introduce a ban on large cruise ships visiting the city. A 2013 ban would have allowed only cruise ships smaller than 40,000-gross tons to enter the Giudecca Canal and St Mark\'s basin.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In January, a regional court scrapped the ban, but some global cruise lines indicated that they would continue to respect it until a long-term solution for the protection of Venice is found.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>For example, P&amp;O Cruises removed Venice from its summer schedule, Holland America moved one of its ships from this area to Alaska and Cunard is reducing (in 2017 and further in 2018) the number of visits by its ships.  As a result, the Venice Port Authority estimated an 11.4 percent drop in cruise ships arriving in 2017 versus 2016, leading to a similar reduction in income for Venice.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gondola_convoy,_Grand_Canal,_Venice.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Gondola_convoy%2C_Grand_Canal%2C_Venice.jpg/220px-Gondola_convoy%2C_Grand_Canal%2C_Venice.jpg" width="220" height="99" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Gondola_convoy%2C_Grand_Canal%2C_Venice.jpg/330px-Gondola_convoy%2C_Grand_Canal%2C_Venice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Gondola_convoy%2C_Grand_Canal%2C_Venice.jpg/440px-Gondola_convoy%2C_Grand_Canal%2C_Venice.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3520" data-file-height="1577" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gondola_convoy,_Grand_Canal,_Venice.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gondoliers on the Grand Canal</div></div></div>\n<p>The city also considered a ban on <a href="/wiki/Wheel" title="Wheel">wheeled</a> <a href="/wiki/Suitcase" title="Suitcase">suitcases</a>, but settled on banning hard wheels for cargo from May 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In addition to accelerating erosion of the ancient city\'s foundations and creating some pollution in the lagoon,<sup id="cite_ref-news.nationalgeographic.com_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news.nationalgeographic.com-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> cruise ships dropping an excessive number of day trippers can make St. Marks Square and other popular attractions too crowded to walk through during the peak season. Government officials see little value to the economy from the "eat and flee" tourists who stay for less than a day, which is typical of those from cruise ships.<sup id="cite_ref-express.co.uk_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-express.co.uk-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Having failed in its 2013 bid to ban oversized cruise ships from the Giudecca canal, the city switched to a new strategy in mid 2017, banning the creation of any additional hotels; currently there are over 24,000 hotel rooms. (The ban does not affect short term rentals in the historic center which is causing an increase in rent for the native residents of Venice.)<sup id="cite_ref-theguardian.com_59-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theguardian.com-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The city had already banned any additional fast food "take-away" outlets to retain the historic character of the city; this was another reason for freezing the number of hotel rooms.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Less than half the millions of annual visitors stay overnight, however.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph.co.uk_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph.co.uk-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-independent.co.uk_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent.co.uk-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guggenheim_Venedig-DSC_0053w.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Guggenheim_Venedig-DSC_0053w.jpg/220px-Guggenheim_Venedig-DSC_0053w.jpg" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Guggenheim_Venedig-DSC_0053w.jpg/330px-Guggenheim_Venedig-DSC_0053w.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Guggenheim_Venedig-DSC_0053w.jpg/440px-Guggenheim_Venedig-DSC_0053w.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3317" data-file-height="1910" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guggenheim_Venedig-DSC_0053w.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Peggy_Guggenheim_Collection" title="Peggy Guggenheim Collection">Venice Guggenheim Museum</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Some locals were aggressively lobbying for new methods that would reduce the number of cruise ship passengers; their estimate indicated that there are up to 30,000 such sightseers per day at peak periods,<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> while other concentrate their effort on promoting a more responsible way of visiting the city.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> An unofficial referendum to ban large cruise ships was held in June 2017. More than 18,000 people voted at 60 polling booths set up by activists and 17,874 chose to favor the ban on ships from the lagoon. The population of Venice at the time was about 50,000.<sup id="cite_ref-express.co.uk_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-express.co.uk-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The organizers of the referendum backed a plan to build a new cruise ship terminal at one of the three entrances to the <a href="/wiki/Venetian_Lagoon" title="Venetian Lagoon">Venetian Lagoon</a>. Passengers would be transferred to smaller boats to take them to the historic area.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, the United Nations warned the city that it may be placed on UNESCO\xe2\x80\x99s list of World Heritage In Danger sites unless cruise ships are banned from the canals near the historic centre.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2017, an official Comitatone released a specific plan to keep the largest cruise ships away from the Piazza San Marco and the entrance to the Grand Canal.\n<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Ships over 55,000 tons will be required to follow a specified path through another canal to a new passenger port to be built in <a href="/wiki/Marghera" title="Marghera">Marghera</a>, an industrial area of the mainland. According to the officials, it will take four years in total to work on the project. However, a lobby group, \'<i>No Grandi Navi</i>\' (No big Ships), argued that the effects of pollution caused by the ships can not be diminished.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_words_of_Venetian_origin">Foreign words of Venetian origin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Foreign words of Venetian origin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Some words with a Venetian etymology include <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/arsenal" class="extiw" title="wikt:arsenal">arsenal</a>, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ciao" class="extiw" title="wikt:ciao">ciao</a>, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ghetto" class="extiw" title="wikt:ghetto">ghetto</a>, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/gondola" class="extiw" title="wikt:gondola">gondola</a>, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/imbroglio" class="extiw" title="wikt:imbroglio">imbroglio</a>, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/lagoon" class="extiw" title="wikt:lagoon">lagoon</a>, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/lazaret" class="extiw" title="wikt:lazaret">lazaret</a>, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/lido" class="extiw" title="wikt:lido">lido</a>, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Montenegro" class="extiw" title="wikt:Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, and <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/regatta" class="extiw" title="wikt:regatta">regatta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The name "<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Venezuela" class="extiw" title="wikt:Venezuela">Venezuela</a>" is a Spanish diminutive of Venice (<i>Veneziola</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Many additional places around the world are named after Venice, e.g., <a href="/wiki/Venice,_Los_Angeles" title="Venice, Los Angeles">Venice, Los Angeles</a>, home of Venice Beach; <a href="/wiki/Venice,_Alberta" title="Venice, Alberta">Venice, Alberta</a> in Canada; <a href="/wiki/Venice,_Florida" title="Venice, Florida">Venice, Florida</a>, a city in Sarasota County; <a href="/wiki/Venice,_New_York" title="Venice, New York">Venice, New York</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_the_historic_centre">In the historic centre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: In the historic centre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Venice_as_seen_from_the_air_with_bridge_to_mainland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Venice_as_seen_from_the_air_with_bridge_to_mainland.jpg/220px-Venice_as_seen_from_the_air_with_bridge_to_mainland.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Venice_as_seen_from_the_air_with_bridge_to_mainland.jpg/330px-Venice_as_seen_from_the_air_with_bridge_to_mainland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Venice_as_seen_from_the_air_with_bridge_to_mainland.jpg/440px-Venice_as_seen_from_the_air_with_bridge_to_mainland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Venice_as_seen_from_the_air_with_bridge_to_mainland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view of Venice including the <i><a href="/wiki/Ponte_della_Libert%C3%A0" title="Ponte della Libert\xc3\xa0">Ponte della Libert\xc3\xa0</a></i> bridge to the mainland.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Giudecca_Canal,_view_from_St_Mark%27s_Campanile.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Giudecca_Canal%2C_view_from_St_Mark%27s_Campanile.jpg/220px-Giudecca_Canal%2C_view_from_St_Mark%27s_Campanile.jpg" width="220" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Giudecca_Canal%2C_view_from_St_Mark%27s_Campanile.jpg/330px-Giudecca_Canal%2C_view_from_St_Mark%27s_Campanile.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Giudecca_Canal%2C_view_from_St_Mark%27s_Campanile.jpg/440px-Giudecca_Canal%2C_view_from_St_Mark%27s_Campanile.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3996" data-file-height="2140" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Giudecca_Canal,_view_from_St_Mark%27s_Campanile.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Giudecca_Canal" title="Giudecca Canal">Giudecca Canal</a>. View from <a href="/wiki/St_Mark%27s_Campanile" title="St Mark&#39;s Campanile">St Mark\'s Campanile</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paolo_Monti_-_Serie_fotografica_(Venezia,_1965)_-_Sandolo_-_BEIC_6343165.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Paolo_Monti_-_Serie_fotografica_%28Venezia%2C_1965%29_-_Sandolo_-_BEIC_6343165.jpg/220px-Paolo_Monti_-_Serie_fotografica_%28Venezia%2C_1965%29_-_Sandolo_-_BEIC_6343165.jpg" width="220" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Paolo_Monti_-_Serie_fotografica_%28Venezia%2C_1965%29_-_Sandolo_-_BEIC_6343165.jpg/330px-Paolo_Monti_-_Serie_fotografica_%28Venezia%2C_1965%29_-_Sandolo_-_BEIC_6343165.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Paolo_Monti_-_Serie_fotografica_%28Venezia%2C_1965%29_-_Sandolo_-_BEIC_6343165.jpg/440px-Paolo_Monti_-_Serie_fotografica_%28Venezia%2C_1965%29_-_Sandolo_-_BEIC_6343165.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1198" data-file-height="1165" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paolo_Monti_-_Serie_fotografica_(Venezia,_1965)_-_Sandolo_-_BEIC_6343165.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sandolo in a picture of <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Monti" title="Paolo Monti">Paolo Monti</a> of 1965. Fondo Paolo Monti, <a href="/wiki/Biblioteca_europea_di_informazione_e_cultura" title="Biblioteca europea di informazione e cultura">BEIC</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:P_%26_O_steamer_in_Venice_circa_1870,_in_album_owned_by_W.F._de_Salis,_a_director_of_the_company.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/96/P_%26_O_steamer_in_Venice_circa_1870%2C_in_album_owned_by_W.F._de_Salis%2C_a_director_of_the_company.jpg/220px-P_%26_O_steamer_in_Venice_circa_1870%2C_in_album_owned_by_W.F._de_Salis%2C_a_director_of_the_company.jpg" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/96/P_%26_O_steamer_in_Venice_circa_1870%2C_in_album_owned_by_W.F._de_Salis%2C_a_director_of_the_company.jpg/330px-P_%26_O_steamer_in_Venice_circa_1870%2C_in_album_owned_by_W.F._de_Salis%2C_a_director_of_the_company.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/96/P_%26_O_steamer_in_Venice_circa_1870%2C_in_album_owned_by_W.F._de_Salis%2C_a_director_of_the_company.jpg/440px-P_%26_O_steamer_in_Venice_circa_1870%2C_in_album_owned_by_W.F._de_Salis%2C_a_director_of_the_company.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3192" data-file-height="2332" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:P_%26_O_steamer_in_Venice_circa_1870,_in_album_owned_by_W.F._de_Salis,_a_director_of_the_company.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/P%26O_(company)" title="P&amp;O (company)">P &amp; O</a> steamer, circa 1870.</div></div></div>\n<p>Venice is built on an <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> of 118 islands<sup id="cite_ref-whc.unesco.org_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whc.unesco.org-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> formed by 177 canals in a shallow lagoon, connected by 409 bridges.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> In the old centre, the canals serve the function of roads, and almost every form of transport is on water or on foot. In the 19th century, a causeway to the mainland brought the <a href="/wiki/Venezia_Santa_Lucia_railway_station" title="Venezia Santa Lucia railway station">Venezia Santa Lucia railway station</a> to Venice, and the <a href="/wiki/Ponte_della_Libert%C3%A0" title="Ponte della Libert\xc3\xa0">Ponte della Libert\xc3\xa0</a> road causeway and parking facilities (in Tronchetto island and in piazzale Roma) were built during the 20th century. Beyond the road and rail land entrances at the northern edge of the city, transportation within the city remains (as it was in centuries past) entirely on water or on foot. Venice is Europe\'s largest urban <a href="/wiki/Auto-free_zones" class="mw-redirect" title="Auto-free zones">car-free area</a>. Venice is unique in Europe, in having remained a sizable functioning city in the 21st century entirely without motorcars or trucks.\n</p><p>The classical Venetian boat is the <a href="/wiki/Gondola" title="Gondola">gondola</a>, (plural: gondole) although it is now mostly used for tourists, or for weddings, funerals, or other ceremonies, or as \'traghetti\' (sing.: traghetto) to cross the Canale Grande in the absence of a nearby bridge. The traghetti are operated by two oarsmen; for some years there were seven such boats but by 2017, only three remained.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are approximately 400 licensed gondoliers in Venice in their distinctive regalia and a similar number of the boats, down from 10,000 that travelled the canals two centuries ago.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ricksteves.com_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ricksteves.com-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Many gondolas are lushly appointed with crushed velvet seats and Persian rugs. Less well-known is the smaller <a href="/wiki/Sandolo" title="Sandolo">sandolo</a>. At the front of each gondola that works in the city, there is a large piece of metal called the <i>f\xc3\xa8ro</i> (iron). Its shape has evolved through the centuries, as documented in many well-known paintings. Its form, topped by a likeness of the Doge\'s hat, became gradually standardized, and was then fixed by local law. It consists of six bars pointing forward representing the Sestieri of the city, and one that points backward representing the <a href="/wiki/Giudecca" title="Giudecca">Giudecca</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ricksteves.com_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ricksteves.com-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Waterways">Waterways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Waterways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rialto_Gondoliers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Rialto_Gondoliers.jpg/220px-Rialto_Gondoliers.jpg" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Rialto_Gondoliers.jpg/330px-Rialto_Gondoliers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Rialto_Gondoliers.jpg/440px-Rialto_Gondoliers.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3592" data-file-height="2512" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rialto_Gondoliers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Rialto_Bridge" title="Rialto Bridge">Rialto Bridge</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Venice is a city of small islands, enhanced during the Middle Ages by the dredging of soils to raise the marshy ground above the tides. The resulting canals encouraged the flourishing of a nautical culture which proved central to the economy of the city. Today those canals still provide the means for transport of goods and people within the city.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:View_from_the_Bridge_of_Sighs_(Ponte_dei_Sospiri),_Venice_Italy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/View_from_the_Bridge_of_Sighs_%28Ponte_dei_Sospiri%29%2C_Venice_Italy.jpg/220px-View_from_the_Bridge_of_Sighs_%28Ponte_dei_Sospiri%29%2C_Venice_Italy.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/View_from_the_Bridge_of_Sighs_%28Ponte_dei_Sospiri%29%2C_Venice_Italy.jpg/330px-View_from_the_Bridge_of_Sighs_%28Ponte_dei_Sospiri%29%2C_Venice_Italy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/View_from_the_Bridge_of_Sighs_%28Ponte_dei_Sospiri%29%2C_Venice_Italy.jpg/440px-View_from_the_Bridge_of_Sighs_%28Ponte_dei_Sospiri%29%2C_Venice_Italy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2700" data-file-height="1802" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:View_from_the_Bridge_of_Sighs_(Ponte_dei_Sospiri),_Venice_Italy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gondolas from the <a href="/wiki/Bridge_of_Sighs" title="Bridge of Sighs">Bridge of Sighs</a> (Ponte dei Sospiri)</div></div></div>\n<p>The maze of canals threaded through the city requires the use of more than 400 bridges to permit the flow of foot traffic. In 2011, the city opened <a href="/wiki/Ponte_della_Costituzione" title="Ponte della Costituzione">Ponte della Costituzione</a>, the fourth bridge across the Grand Canal, connecting the <a href="/wiki/Piazzale_Roma" title="Piazzale Roma">Piazzale Roma</a> bus terminal area with the Stazione Ferroviaria (train station), the others being the original <a href="/wiki/Ponte_di_Rialto" class="mw-redirect" title="Ponte di Rialto">Ponte di Rialto</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ponte_dell%27Accademia" title="Ponte dell&#39;Accademia">Ponte dell\'Accademia</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Ponte_degli_Scalzi" title="Ponte degli Scalzi">Ponte degli Scalzi</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">Public transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Public transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Azienda_del_Consorzio_Trasporti_Veneziano" class="mw-redirect" title="Azienda del Consorzio Trasporti Veneziano">Azienda del Consorzio Trasporti Veneziano</a> (ACTV) is a public company responsible for public transportation in Venice.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Waterbus_routes_in_Venezia_map.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Waterbus_routes_in_Venezia_map.jpg/220px-Waterbus_routes_in_Venezia_map.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Waterbus_routes_in_Venezia_map.jpg/330px-Waterbus_routes_in_Venezia_map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Waterbus_routes_in_Venezia_map.jpg/440px-Waterbus_routes_in_Venezia_map.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="2268" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Waterbus_routes_in_Venezia_map.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of the waterbus routes in Venezia</div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lagoon_area">Lagoon area</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Lagoon area">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The main public transportation means are motorised <a href="/wiki/Waterbus" class="mw-redirect" title="Waterbus">waterbuses</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Vaporetto" title="Vaporetto">vaporetti</a></i>) which ply regular routes along the Grand Canal and between the city\'s islands. The only gondole still in common use by Venetians are the <i>traghetti</i>, foot passenger <a href="/wiki/Ferry" title="Ferry">ferries</a> crossing the Grand Canal at certain points without bridges. Other gondole target tourists on an hourly basis.<sup id="cite_ref-ricksteves.com_87-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ricksteves.com-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Venice_People_Mover" title="Venice People Mover">Venice People Mover</a> (managed by ASM) is a <a href="/wiki/Cable_railway" title="Cable railway">cable</a>-operated <a href="/wiki/Public_transit" class="mw-redirect" title="Public transit">public transit</a> system connecting <a href="/wiki/Tronchetto_island" class="mw-redirect" title="Tronchetto island">Tronchetto island</a> with Piazzale Roma. Water taxis are also active.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lido_and_Pellestrina_islands">Lido and Pellestrina islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Lido and Pellestrina islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Lido_di_Venezia" title="Lido di Venezia">Lido</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pellestrina" title="Pellestrina">Pellestrina</a> are two islands forming a barrier between the southern Venetian Lagoon and the Adriatic Sea. In those islands, road traffic is allowed. There are bus services on islands and waterbus services linking islands with other islands (Venice, <a href="/wiki/Murano" title="Murano">Murano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burano" title="Burano">Burano</a>) and with the peninsula of <a href="/wiki/Cavallino-Treporti" title="Cavallino-Treporti">Cavallino-Treporti</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mainland">Mainland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Mainland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The mainland of Venice is composed of 5 boroughs: <a href="/wiki/Mestre" title="Mestre">Mestre</a>-Carpenedo, <a href="/wiki/Marghera" title="Marghera">Marghera</a>, Chirignago-Zelarino and Favaro Veneto. Mestre is the center and the most populated urban area of the mainland of Venice. There are several bus routes and two <a href="/wiki/Translohr" title="Translohr">Translohr</a> <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Mestre" title="Trams in Mestre">tramway lines</a>. Several bus routes and one of the above tramway lines link the mainland with <i><a href="/wiki/Piazzale_Roma" title="Piazzale Roma">Piazzale Roma</a></i>, the main bus station in Venice, via <a href="/wiki/Ponte_della_Libert%C3%A0" title="Ponte della Libert\xc3\xa0">Ponte della Libert\xc3\xa0</a>, a road bridge connecting the mainland with the group of islands that comprise the historic center of Venice.\nThe average amount of time people spend commuting with public transit in Venice, for example to and from work, on a weekday is 52 min. 12.2% of public transit riders, ride for more than 2 hours every day. The average amount of time people wait at a stop or station for public transit is 10 min, while 17.6% of riders wait for over 20 minutes on average every day. The average distance people usually ride in a single trip with public transit is 7&#160;km, while 12% travel for over 12&#160;km in a single direction.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:38px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vaporetti_Venice_Lagoon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" class="gallerytext">\n<p>Vaporetti (water buses) provide the primary means of transportation\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:31.5px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:IRISBUS_ACTV_in_Mestre.jpg" class="image"><img data-file-height="2000" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Mestre" title="Trams in Mestre">Tram in Venice</a> leaving <a href="/wiki/Piazzale_Roma" title="Piazzale Roma">Piazzale Roma</a>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trains">Trains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Trains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Venezia_Santa_Lucia_Train_Station_R02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Venezia_Santa_Lucia_Train_Station_R02.jpg/220px-Venezia_Santa_Lucia_Train_Station_R02.jpg" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Venezia_Santa_Lucia_Train_Station_R02.jpg/330px-Venezia_Santa_Lucia_Train_Station_R02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Venezia_Santa_Lucia_Train_Station_R02.jpg/440px-Venezia_Santa_Lucia_Train_Station_R02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4860" data-file-height="2920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Venezia_Santa_Lucia_Train_Station_R02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Venezia_Santa_Lucia_railway_station" title="Venezia Santa Lucia railway station">Venice St Lucia station</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Venice has regional and national trains, including trains to Florence (1h53), Rome (3h33), Naples (4h50), Milan (2h13) and Turin (3h10). In addition there are international day trains to Zurich, Innsbruck, Munich and Vienna, plus overnight sleeper services to Paris and Dijon (Thello), Munich and Vienna (\xc3\x96BB).\n</p>\n<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Venezia_Santa_Lucia_railway_station" title="Venezia Santa Lucia railway station">St Lucia station</a> is a few steps away from a vaporetti stop in the historic city next to <i>Piazzale Roma</i>. As well as many more local trains, this station is the terminus of the luxury Venice Simplon Orient Express from Paris and London.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Venezia_Mestre_railway_station" title="Venezia Mestre railway station">Mestre station</a> is on the mainland, on the border between the boroughs of Mestre and Marghera.</li></ul>\n<p>Both stations are managed by Grandi Stazioni; they are linked by the <i>Ponte della Libert\xc3\xa0</i> (Liberty Bridge) between the mainland and the islands.\n</p><p>Others small stations in the municipality are: Venezia Porto Marghera, Venezia Carpenedo, Venezia Mestre Ospedale, Venezia Mestre Porta Ovest.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ports">Ports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Ports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2017_06_Venezia_Terminal_Passeggeri_Terminal_Passeggeri_2860.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/2017_06_Venezia_Terminal_Passeggeri_Terminal_Passeggeri_2860.jpg/220px-2017_06_Venezia_Terminal_Passeggeri_Terminal_Passeggeri_2860.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/2017_06_Venezia_Terminal_Passeggeri_Terminal_Passeggeri_2860.jpg/330px-2017_06_Venezia_Terminal_Passeggeri_Terminal_Passeggeri_2860.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/2017_06_Venezia_Terminal_Passeggeri_Terminal_Passeggeri_2860.jpg/440px-2017_06_Venezia_Terminal_Passeggeri_Terminal_Passeggeri_2860.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2017_06_Venezia_Terminal_Passeggeri_Terminal_Passeggeri_2860.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">Cruise ships</a> at the passenger terminal in the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Venice" title="Port of Venice">Port of Venice</a> (<i>Venezia Terminal Passeggeri</i>)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aeroporto_di_Venezia_-_vue_aerienne.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Aeroporto_di_Venezia_-_vue_aerienne.jpg/220px-Aeroporto_di_Venezia_-_vue_aerienne.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Aeroporto_di_Venezia_-_vue_aerienne.jpg/330px-Aeroporto_di_Venezia_-_vue_aerienne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Aeroporto_di_Venezia_-_vue_aerienne.jpg/440px-Aeroporto_di_Venezia_-_vue_aerienne.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1022" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aeroporto_di_Venezia_-_vue_aerienne.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Marco Polo International Airport">Marco Polo International Airport</a> (<i>Aeroporto di Venezia <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">Marco Polo</a></i>)</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Venice" title="Port of Venice">Port of Venice</a> (<a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <i lang="it">Porto di Venezia</i>)  is the eighth-busiest commercial port in Italy and is one of the most important in the Mediterranean concerning the cruise sector, as a major hub for <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">cruise ships</a>. It is one of the major Italian ports and is included in the list of the leading European ports which are located on the strategic nodes of trans-European networks. In 2006, 30,936,931 tonnes passed through the port, of which 14,541,961 was the commercial sector, and saw 1,453,513 passengers. In 2002, the port handled 262,337 containers.<sup id="cite_ref-FletcherSpencer2005_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FletcherSpencer2005-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Venice is served by the <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Marco Polo International Airport">Marco Polo International Airport</a> (<i>Aeroporto di Venezia <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">Marco Polo</a></i>), named in honor of its noted citizen. The airport is on the mainland and was rebuilt away from the coast. Public transport from the airport takes one to:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Venice <a href="/wiki/Piazzale_Roma" title="Piazzale Roma">Piazzale Roma</a> by ATVO (provincial company) buses<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> and by ACTV (city company) buses (route 5 <i>aerobus</i>);<sup id="cite_ref-actv.it_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-actv.it-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Venice, Lido and Murano by Alilaguna (private company) motor boats;</li>\n<li>Mestre, the mainland and Venice Mestre railway station (convenient for connections to <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Padova" class="mw-redirect" title="Padova">Padova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trieste" title="Trieste">Trieste</a>, <a href="/wiki/Verona" title="Verona">Verona</a> and the rest of Italy) by ACTV lines (route 15 and 45)<sup id="cite_ref-actv.it_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-actv.it-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> and by ATVO lines;</li>\n<li>regional destinations (Treviso, Padua, the beach, ...) by ATVO buses and by Busitalia Sita Nord<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> buses (national company).</li></ul>\n<p>Some airlines market <a href="/wiki/Treviso_Airport" title="Treviso Airport">Treviso Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Treviso" title="Treviso">Treviso</a>, 30 kilometres (19&#160;mi) from Venice, as a Venice gateway. Some simply advertise flights to "Venice", while naming the actual airport only in small print.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> There are public buses from this airport to Venice.\n</p><p>Venezia-Lido "Giovanni Nicelli",<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> a public airport suitable for smaller aircraft, is at the NE end of <a href="/wiki/Lido_di_Venezia" title="Lido di Venezia">Lido di Venezia</a>. It has a 994-metre grass runway.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The most Venetian sport is probably the "<i>Voga alla Veneta</i>", also commonly called, "Voga Veneta". The Venetian Rowing is a technique invented in the Venetian Lagoon which has the particularity to see the rower(s), one or more, rowing standing looking forward. Today, the <i>Voga alla Veneta</i> is not only the way the Gondolier row tourists around Venice but also the way Venetians row for pleasure and sport. Many races called <i>regata(e)</i> happen throughought the year.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> The culminating event of the rowing season is the day of the "Regata Storica", happening on the first Sunday of September each year.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The main football club in the city is <a href="/wiki/Venezia_F.C." title="Venezia F.C.">Venezia F.C.</a>, founded in 1907, which currently plays in the <a href="/wiki/Serie_B" title="Serie B">Serie B</a>. Their ground, the <a href="/wiki/Stadio_Pierluigi_Penzo" title="Stadio Pierluigi Penzo">Stadio Pierluigi Penzo</a> situated in <a href="/wiki/Sant%27Elena" title="Sant&#39;Elena">Sant\'Elena</a>, is one of the oldest venues in Italy.\n</p><p>The local basketball club is <a href="/wiki/Reyer_Venezia_Mestre" class="mw-redirect" title="Reyer Venezia Mestre">Reyer Venezia Mestre</a>, founded in 1872 as gymnastics club <i>Societ\xc3\xa0 Sportiva Costantino Reyer</i>, and in 1907 as basketball club. Reyer currently plays in the <a href="/wiki/Lega_Basket_Serie_A" title="Lega Basket Serie A">Lega Basket Serie A</a>. The men\'s team won the Italian Championships in 1942, 1943 and 2017. Their arena is the <a href="/wiki/Palasport_Giuseppe_Taliercio" title="Palasport Giuseppe Taliercio">Palasport Giuseppe Taliercio</a> situated in <a href="/wiki/Mestre" title="Mestre">Mestre</a>. <a href="/wiki/Luigi_Brugnaro" title="Luigi Brugnaro">Luigi Brugnaro</a> is both the president of the club and the mayor of the city.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:C%C3%A0_Foscari_and_Giustinian_palaces_from_San_Toma%27.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/C%C3%A0_Foscari_and_Giustinian_palaces_from_San_Toma%27.JPG/220px-C%C3%A0_Foscari_and_Giustinian_palaces_from_San_Toma%27.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/C%C3%A0_Foscari_and_Giustinian_palaces_from_San_Toma%27.JPG/330px-C%C3%A0_Foscari_and_Giustinian_palaces_from_San_Toma%27.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/C%C3%A0_Foscari_and_Giustinian_palaces_from_San_Toma%27.JPG/440px-C%C3%A0_Foscari_and_Giustinian_palaces_from_San_Toma%27.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:C%C3%A0_Foscari_and_Giustinian_palaces_from_San_Toma%27.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ca%27_Foscari_University_of_Venice" title="Ca&#39; Foscari University of Venice">Ca\' Foscari University of Venice</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Venice is a major international centre for higher education. The city hosts the <a href="/wiki/Ca%27_Foscari_University_of_Venice" title="Ca&#39; Foscari University of Venice">Ca\' Foscari University of Venice</a>, founded in 1868;<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A0_Iuav_di_Venezia" title="Universit\xc3\xa0 Iuav di Venezia">Universit\xc3\xa0 Iuav di Venezia</a>, founded in 1926;<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Venice_International_University" title="Venice International University">Venice International University</a>, an international research center, founded in 1995 and located on the island of <a href="/wiki/San_Servolo" title="San Servolo">San Servolo</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> and the EIUC-European Inter-University Centre for Human Rights and Democratisation, located on the island of Lido di Venezia.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other Venetian institutions of higher education are: the "Accademia di Belle Arti" (Academy of Fine Arts), established in 1750, whose first Chairman was <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Piazzetta" title="Giovanni Battista Piazzetta">Giovanni Battista Piazzetta</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Conservatorio_di_Musica_Benedetto_Marcello_di_Venezia" title="Conservatorio di Musica Benedetto Marcello di Venezia">Benedetto Marcello Conservatory of Music</a>, which, established in 1876 as High School and Musical Society, later (1915) became "Liceo Musicale" and finally (1940), when its Director was <a href="/wiki/Gian_Francesco_Malipiero" title="Gian Francesco Malipiero">Gian Francesco Malipiero</a>, State Conservatory of Music.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 0.5em;"><tbody><tr><th class="navbox-title" colspan="3" style="padding:0.25em;font-size:110%">Historical population</th></tr><tr style="font-size:95%"><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;width:3em">Year</th><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px 2px;text-align:right"><abbr
