style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1200 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">80,000</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+33.3%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1300 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">180,000</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+125.0%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1400 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">110,000</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">\xe2\x88\x9238.9%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">1423 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">150,000</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">+36.4%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1500 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">100,000</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">\xe2\x88\x9233.3%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1560 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">170,000</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+70.0%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1600 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">200,000</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+17.6%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1700 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">140,000</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">\xe2\x88\x9230.0%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1800 </th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">140,000</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+0.0%</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Venice_city_scenes_-_on_the_Grand_Canal_-_Polizia!_(11002248065).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Venice_city_scenes_-_on_the_Grand_Canal_-_Polizia%21_%2811002248065%29.jpg/220px-Venice_city_scenes_-_on_the_Grand_Canal_-_Polizia%21_%2811002248065%29.jpg" width="220" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Venice_city_scenes_-_on_the_Grand_Canal_-_Polizia%21_%2811002248065%29.jpg/330px-Venice_city_scenes_-_on_the_Grand_Canal_-_Polizia%21_%2811002248065%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Venice_city_scenes_-_on_the_Grand_Canal_-_Polizia%21_%2811002248065%29.jpg/440px-Venice_city_scenes_-_on_the_Grand_Canal_-_Polizia%21_%2811002248065%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1605" data-file-height="1867" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Venice_city_scenes_-_on_the_Grand_Canal_-_Polizia!_(11002248065).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_della_Salute" title="Santa Maria della Salute">Santa Maria della Salute</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The city was one of the largest in Europe in the <a href="/wiki/High_Middle_Ages" title="High Middle Ages">High Middle Ages</a>, with a population of 60,000 in AD 1000; 80,000 in 1200; and rising up to 110,000\xe2\x80\x93180,000 in 1300. In the mid 1500s the city\'s population was 170,000, and by 1600 almost 200,000.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2009, there were 270,098 people residing in Venice\'s comune (the population estimate of 272,000 inhabitants includes the population of the whole Comune of Venezia; around 60,000 in the historic city of Venice (Centro storico); 176,000 in Terraferma (the Mainland); and 31,000 live on other islands in the lagoon), of whom 47.4% were male and 52.6% were female. Minors (children ages 18 and younger) were 14.36% of the population compared to pensioners who numbered 25.7%. This compared with the Italian average of 18.06% (minors) and 19.94% (pensioners). The average age of Venice residents was 46 compared to the Italian average of 42. In the five years between 2002 and 2007, the population of Venice declined by 0.2%, while Italy as a whole grew by 3.85%.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The population in the historic old city declined much faster: from about 120,000 in 1980 to about 60,000 in 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> and to below 55,000 in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of  2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, 91% of the population was Italian. The largest immigrant group came from other European nations: (<a href="/wiki/Romanians" title="Romanians">Romanians</a>, the largest group: 3%, South Asia: 1.3%, and East Asia: 0.9%).\n</p><p>Venice is predominantly <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a> (92.7% of resident population in the area of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Venice" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Venice">Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Venice</a> in 2012<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>), but because of the long-standing relationship with <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a>, there is also a noticeable <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox</a> presence, and as a result of immigration, there are now some <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Muslim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a> inhabitants.\n</p><p>Since 1991 the Church of <a href="/wiki/San_Giorgio_dei_Greci" title="San Giorgio dei Greci">San Giorgio dei Greci</a> in Venice has become the <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_see" title="Episcopal see">see</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Archdiocese_of_Italy_and_Malta" title="Greek Orthodox Archdiocese of Italy and Malta">Greek Orthodox Archdiocese of Italy and Malta and Exarchate of Southern Europe</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Rite" title="Byzantine Rite">Byzantine-rite</a> diocese under the <a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_Patriarchate_of_Constantinople" title="Ecumenical Patriarchate of Constantinople">Ecumenical Patriarchate of Constantinople</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There is also a historic <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Venice" title="History of the Jews in Venice">Jewish community</a> in Venice. The <a href="/wiki/Venetian_Ghetto" title="Venetian Ghetto">Venetian Ghetto</a> was the area in which Jews were compelled to live under the Venetian Republic. The word <i>ghetto</i>, originally <a href="/wiki/Venetian_language" title="Venetian language">Venetian</a>, is now used in many languages. <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">Shakespeare</a>\'s play <i><a href="/wiki/The_Merchant_of_Venice" title="The Merchant of Venice">The Merchant of Venice</a></i>, written in the late 16th century, features <a href="/wiki/Shylock" title="Shylock">Shylock</a>, a Venetian Jew. The first complete and uncensored printed edition of the <a href="/wiki/Talmud" title="Talmud">Talmud</a> was printed in Venice by <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Bomberg" title="Daniel Bomberg">Daniel Bomberg</a> in 1523. During World War II Jews were rounded up in Venice and deported to <a href="/wiki/Extermination_camp" title="Extermination camp">extermination camps</a>. Since the end of the war the Jewish population of Venice has declined from 1500 to about 500. Only around 30 Jews live in the former ghetto which houses the city\'s major Jewish institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> In modern times, Venice has an <a href="/wiki/Eruv" title="Eruv">eruv</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> used by the Jewish community.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Venetian_literature" title="Venetian literature">Venetian literature</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marco_Polo,_Il_Milione,_Chapter_CXXIII_and_CXXIV.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Marco_Polo%2C_Il_Milione%2C_Chapter_CXXIII_and_CXXIV.jpg/220px-Marco_Polo%2C_Il_Milione%2C_Chapter_CXXIII_and_CXXIV.jpg" width="220" height="318" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Marco_Polo%2C_Il_Milione%2C_Chapter_CXXIII_and_CXXIV.jpg/330px-Marco_Polo%2C_Il_Milione%2C_Chapter_CXXIII_and_CXXIV.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Marco_Polo%2C_Il_Milione%2C_Chapter_CXXIII_and_CXXIV.jpg/440px-Marco_Polo%2C_Il_Milione%2C_Chapter_CXXIII_and_CXXIV.jpg 2x" data-file-width="982" data-file-height="1419" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marco_Polo,_Il_Milione,_Chapter_CXXIII_and_CXXIV.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/The_Travels_of_Marco_Polo" title="The Travels of Marco Polo">The Travels of Marco Polo</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Venice has long been a source of inspiration for authors, playwrights, and poets, and at the forefront of the technological development of printing and publishing.\n</p><p>Two of the most noted Venetian writers were <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">Marco Polo</a> in the Middle Ages and later <a href="/wiki/Giacomo_Casanova" title="Giacomo Casanova">Giacomo Casanova</a>. Polo (1254\xe2\x80\x931324) was a merchant who voyaged to <a href="/wiki/The_Orient" class="mw-redirect" title="The Orient">the Orient</a>. His series of books, co-written by <a href="/wiki/Rustichello_da_Pisa" title="Rustichello da Pisa">Rustichello da Pisa</a> and titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Travels_of_Marco_Polo" title="The Travels of Marco Polo">Il Milione</a></i> provided important knowledge of the lands east of Europe, from the Middle East to China, Japan, and Russia. <a href="/wiki/Giacomo_Casanova" title="Giacomo Casanova">Giacomo Casanova</a> (1725\xe2\x80\x931798) was a prolific writer and adventurer best remembered for his autobiography, <i>Histoire De Ma Vie</i> (<i>Story of My Life</i>), which links his colourful lifestyle to the city of Venice.\n</p><p>Venetian playwrights followed the old Italian theatre tradition of <i><a href="/wiki/Commedia_dell%27arte" title="Commedia dell&#39;arte">Commedia dell\'arte</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Angelo_Beolco" title="Angelo Beolco">Ruzante</a> (1502\xe2\x80\x931542), <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Goldoni" title="Carlo Goldoni">Carlo Goldoni</a> (1707\xe2\x80\x931793), and <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Gozzi" title="Carlo Gozzi">Carlo Gozzi</a> (1720\xe2\x80\x931806) used the Venetian dialect extensively in their comedies.\n</p><p>Venice has also inspired writers from abroad. Shakespeare set <i><a href="/wiki/Othello" title="Othello">Othello</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Merchant_of_Venice" title="The Merchant of Venice">The Merchant of Venice</a></i> in the city, as did <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Mann" title="Thomas Mann">Thomas Mann</a> with his novel, <i><a href="/wiki/Death_in_Venice" title="Death in Venice">Death in Venice</a></i> (1912). The French writer <a href="/wiki/Philippe_Sollers" title="Philippe Sollers">Philippe Sollers</a> spent most of his life in Venice and published <i> A Dictionary For Lovers Of Venice</i> in 2004.\n</p><p>The city features prominently in <a href="/wiki/Henry_James" title="Henry James">Henry James</a>\' <i><a href="/wiki/The_Aspern_Papers" title="The Aspern Papers">The Aspern Papers</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wings_of_the_Dove" title="The Wings of the Dove">The Wings of the Dove</a></i>. It is also visited in <a href="/wiki/Evelyn_Waugh" title="Evelyn Waugh">Evelyn Waugh</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Brideshead_Revisited" title="Brideshead Revisited">Brideshead Revisited</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Marcel_Proust" title="Marcel Proust">Marcel Proust</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/In_Search_of_Lost_Time" title="In Search of Lost Time">In Search of Lost Time</a></i>. Perhaps the most known children\'s book set in Venice is <i>The Thief Lord</i>, written by the German author <a href="/wiki/Cornelia_Funke" title="Cornelia Funke">Cornelia Funke</a>.\n</p><p>The poet <a href="/wiki/Ugo_Foscolo" title="Ugo Foscolo">Ugo Foscolo</a> (1778\xe2\x80\x931827), born in <a href="/wiki/Zakynthos" title="Zakynthos">Zante</a>, an island that at the time belonged to the Republic of Venice, was also a <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary" title="Revolutionary">revolutionary</a> who wanted to see a free republic established in Venice following its fall to <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>.\n</p><p>Venice also inspired the poetry of <a href="/wiki/Ezra_Pound" title="Ezra Pound">Ezra Pound</a>, who wrote his first literary work in the city. Pound died in 1972, and his remains are buried in Venice\'s cemetery island of <a href="/wiki/Isola_di_San_Michele" title="Isola di San Michele">San Michele</a>.\n</p><p>Venice is also linked to the technological aspects of writing. The city was the location of one of Italy\'s earliest printing presses, established by <a href="/wiki/Aldus_Manutius" title="Aldus Manutius">Aldus Manutius</a> (1449\xe2\x80\x931515).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> From this beginning Venice developed as an important typographic center and even as late as the 18th century was responsible for printing half of Italy\'s published books.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="In_literature_and_adapted_works">In literature and adapted works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: In literature and adapted works">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The city is a particularly popular setting for essays, novels, and other works of fictional or non-fictional literature. Examples of these include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Casanova" class="mw-redirect" title="Casanova">Casanova</a>\'s autobiographical <a href="/wiki/Histoire_de_ma_vie" title="Histoire de ma vie"><i>History of My Life</i></a>,</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ben_Jonson" title="Ben Jonson">Ben Jonson</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Volpone" title="Volpone">Volpone</a></i> (1605\xe2\x80\x936),</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Donna_Leon" title="Donna Leon">Donna Leon</a>\'s Commissario Guido Brunetti <a href="/wiki/Crime_fiction" title="Crime fiction">crime fiction</a> series and cookbook, and the German television series based on the novels</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Anne_Rice" title="Anne Rice">Anne Rice</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Cry_to_Heaven" title="Cry to Heaven">Cry to Heaven</a></i> (1982),</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jacqueline_Carey" title="Jacqueline Carey">Jacqueline Carey</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Kushiel%27s_Chosen" title="Kushiel&#39;s Chosen">Kushiel\'s Chosen</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Historical_fantasy" title="Historical fantasy">historical fantasy</a> or <a href="/wiki/Alternate_history" title="Alternate history">alternate history</a>) A large portion of the novel takes place in a city known as La Serenissima. It is an alternative-history version of Venice, complete with masquerades, canals and a Doge.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Shakespeare" class="mw-redirect" title="Shakespeare">Shakespeare</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Merchant_of_Venice" class="mw-redirect" title="Merchant of Venice">Merchant of Venice</a></i> (ca. 1596\xe2\x80\x931598) and <i><a href="/wiki/Othello" title="Othello">Othello</a></i>,</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Philippe_Sollers" title="Philippe Sollers">Philippe Sollers</a>\' <i><a href="/wiki/Watteau_in_Venice" title="Watteau in Venice">Watteau in Venice</a></i>, and</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Voltaire" title="Voltaire">Voltaire</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Candide" title="Candide">Candide</a></i>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Italo_Calvino" title="Italo Calvino">Italo Calvino</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Invisible_Cities" title="Invisible Cities">Invisible Cities</a>.</li></ul>\n<p>Additionally, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Mann" title="Thomas Mann">Thomas Mann</a>\'s novella, <i><a href="/wiki/Death_in_Venice" title="Death in Venice">Death in Venice</a></i> (1912), was the basis for Benjamin Britten\'s <a href="/wiki/Death_in_Venice_(opera)" title="Death in Venice (opera)">eponymous opera</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_and_printing">Art and printing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Art and printing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Canaletto_-_Bucentaur%27s_return_to_the_pier_by_the_Palazzo_Ducale_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Canaletto_-_Bucentaur%27s_return_to_the_pier_by_the_Palazzo_Ducale_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/220px-Canaletto_-_Bucentaur%27s_return_to_the_pier_by_the_Palazzo_Ducale_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Canaletto_-_Bucentaur%27s_return_to_the_pier_by_the_Palazzo_Ducale_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/330px-Canaletto_-_Bucentaur%27s_return_to_the_pier_by_the_Palazzo_Ducale_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Canaletto_-_Bucentaur%27s_return_to_the_pier_by_the_Palazzo_Ducale_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/440px-Canaletto_-_Bucentaur%27s_return_to_the_pier_by_the_Palazzo_Ducale_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="30000" data-file-height="20857" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Canaletto_-_Bucentaur%27s_return_to_the_pier_by_the_Palazzo_Ducale_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An 18th-century view of Venice by Venetian artist <a href="/wiki/Canaletto" title="Canaletto">Canaletto</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Venice, especially during the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a> periods, was a major centre of art and developed a unique style known as the <a href="/wiki/Venetian_School_(art)" class="mw-redirect" title="Venetian School (art)">Venetian School</a>. In the Middle Ages and the Renaissance, Venice, along with <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a> and Rome, became one of the most important centres of art in Europe, and numerous wealthy Venetians became patrons of the arts. Venice at the time was a rich and prosperous <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Republics" class="mw-redirect" title="Maritime Republics">Maritime Republic</a>, which controlled a vast sea and trade empire.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palazzo_Cavalli-Franchetti_WB.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Palazzo_Cavalli-Franchetti_WB.jpg/220px-Palazzo_Cavalli-Franchetti_WB.jpg" width="220" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Palazzo_Cavalli-Franchetti_WB.jpg/330px-Palazzo_Cavalli-Franchetti_WB.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Palazzo_Cavalli-Franchetti_WB.jpg/440px-Palazzo_Cavalli-Franchetti_WB.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3500" data-file-height="2820" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palazzo_Cavalli-Franchetti_WB.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Cavalli-Franchetti" title="Palazzo Cavalli-Franchetti">Palazzo Cavalli-Franchetti</a> is an example of Venetian Gothic architecture alongside the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Canal_(Venice)" title="Grand Canal (Venice)">Grand Canal</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Venice has a rich and diverse <a href="/wiki/Architectural_style" title="Architectural style">architectural style</a>, the most prominent of which is the <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> style. <a href="/wiki/Venetian_Gothic_architecture" title="Venetian Gothic architecture">Venetian Gothic architecture</a> is a term given to a Venetian building style combining use of the Gothic lancet arch with <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_architecture" title="Byzantine architecture">Byzantine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_architecture" title="Ottoman architecture">Ottoman</a> influences. The style originated in 14th-century Venice, where the confluence of <a href="/wiki/Byzantine" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine">Byzantine</a> style from <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> met Arab influence from <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic Spain">Islamic Spain</a>. Chief examples of the style are the <a href="/wiki/Doge%27s_Palace,_Venice" class="mw-redirect" title="Doge&#39;s Palace, Venice">Doge\'s Palace</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ca%27_d%27Oro" title="Ca&#39; d&#39;Oro">Ca\' d\'Oro</a> in the city. The city also has several <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a> buildings, including the <a href="/wiki/Ca%27_Pesaro" title="Ca&#39; Pesaro">Ca\' Pesaro</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ca%27_Rezzonico" title="Ca&#39; Rezzonico">Ca\' Rezzonico</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ca%27_d%27Oro_facciata.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Ca%27_d%27Oro_facciata.jpg/220px-Ca%27_d%27Oro_facciata.jpg" width="220" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Ca%27_d%27Oro_facciata.jpg/330px-Ca%27_d%27Oro_facciata.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Ca%27_d%27Oro_facciata.jpg/440px-Ca%27_d%27Oro_facciata.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="3750" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ca%27_d%27Oro_facciata.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Ca%27_d%27Oro" title="Ca&#39; d&#39;Oro">Ca\' d\'Oro</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>By the end of the 15th century, Venice had become the European capital of printing, being one of the first cities in Italy (after Subiaco and Rome) to have a printing press after those established in Germany, having 417 printers by 1500. The most important printing office was the <a href="/wiki/Aldine_Press" title="Aldine Press">Aldine Press</a> of <a href="/wiki/Aldus_Manutius" title="Aldus Manutius">Aldus Manutius</a>, which in 1499 printed the <i><a href="/wiki/Hypnerotomachia_Poliphili" title="Hypnerotomachia Poliphili">Hypnerotomachia Poliphili</a></i>, considered the most beautiful book of the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a>, and established modern <a href="/wiki/Punctuation" title="Punctuation">punctuation</a>, the page format and <a href="/wiki/Italic_type" title="Italic type">italic type</a>, and the first printed work of <a href="/wiki/Aristotle" title="Aristotle">Aristotle</a>.\n</p><p>In the 16th century, Venetian painting was developed through influences from the Paduan School and <a href="/wiki/Antonello_da_Messina" title="Antonello da Messina">Antonello da Messina</a>, who introduced the oil painting technique of the <a href="/wiki/Van_Eyck" title="Van Eyck">Van Eyck</a> brothers. It is signified by a warm colour scale and a picturesque use of colour. Early masters were the Bellini and Vivarini families, followed by <a href="/wiki/Giorgione" title="Giorgione">Giorgione</a> and <a href="/wiki/Titian" title="Titian">Titian</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Tintoretto" title="Tintoretto">Tintoretto</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Veronese" title="Paolo Veronese">Veronese</a>. In the early 16th century, there was rivalry in Venetian painting between the <i>disegno</i> and <i>colorito</i> techniques.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Canvas" title="Canvas">Canvases</a> (the common painting surface) originated in Venice during the early Renaissance. These early canvases were generally rough.\n</p><p>In the 18th century, Venetian painting had a revival with <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Tiepolo" title="Giovanni Battista Tiepolo">Tiepolo</a>\'s decorative painting and <a href="/wiki/Canaletto" title="Canaletto">Canaletto</a>\'s and <a href="/wiki/Guardi" class="mw-redirect" title="Guardi">Guardi</a>\'s panoramic views.\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_painters_and_architects_of_Venice" title="List of painters and architects of Venice">List of painters and architects of Venice</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Venetian_School_(art)" class="mw-redirect" title="Venetian School (art)">Venetian School (art)</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Venetian_gothic_architecture">Venetian gothic architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Venetian gothic architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><b>Venetian Gothic</b> is an <a href="/wiki/Architectural_style" title="Architectural style">architectural style</a> combining use of the <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> <a href="/wiki/Lancet_window" title="Lancet window">lancet arch</a> with <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_architecture" title="Byzantine architecture">Byzantine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moorish_architecture" title="Moorish architecture">Moorish</a> influences. The style originated in 14th-century Venice with the confluence of Byzantine styles from <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a>, Moorish influences from <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Al-Andalus</a>, and early Gothic forms from mainland Italy.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Chief examples of the style are the <a href="/wiki/Doge%27s_Palace,_Venice" class="mw-redirect" title="Doge&#39;s Palace, Venice">Doge\'s Palace</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ca%27_d%27Oro" title="Ca&#39; d&#39;Oro">Ca\' d\'Oro</a> in Venice.\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Venetian_Gothic_architecture" title="Venetian Gothic architecture">Venetian Gothic architecture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Medieval_architecture" title="Medieval architecture">Medieval architecture</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hotel_Danieli-dandolo_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Hotel_Danieli-dandolo_2012.jpg/220px-Hotel_Danieli-dandolo_2012.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Hotel_Danieli-dandolo_2012.jpg/330px-Hotel_Danieli-dandolo_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Hotel_Danieli-dandolo_2012.jpg/440px-Hotel_Danieli-dandolo_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hotel_Danieli-dandolo_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Dandolo" class="mw-redirect" title="Palazzo Dandolo">Palazzo Dandolo</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ca%27_Rezzonico_(Venice).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Ca%27_Rezzonico_%28Venice%29.jpg/220px-Ca%27_Rezzonico_%28Venice%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Ca%27_Rezzonico_%28Venice%29.jpg/330px-Ca%27_Rezzonico_%28Venice%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Ca%27_Rezzonico_%28Venice%29.jpg/440px-Ca%27_Rezzonico_%28Venice%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5904" data-file-height="3922" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ca%27_Rezzonico_(Venice).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a> <a href="/wiki/Ca%27_Rezzonico" title="Ca&#39; Rezzonico">Ca\' Rezzonico</a>.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rococo_architectural_style">Rococo architectural style</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Rococo architectural style">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>It can be argued that Venice produced the best and most refined <a href="/wiki/Rococo" title="Rococo">rococo</a> designs. At the time<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (August 2015)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>, Venice was in trouble. It had lost most of its maritime power, was lagging behind its rivals in political importance, and society had become decadent, with nobles wasting their money in gambling and partying. But Venice remained Italy\'s fashion capital, and was a serious contender to Paris in terms of wealth, architecture, luxury, taste, sophistication, trade, decoration, style, and design.<sup id="cite_ref-Miller_2005_p.82_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Miller_2005_p.82-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Venetian rococo was well known as rich and luxurious, with usually very extravagant designs. Unique Venetian furniture pieces included the <i>divani da portego</i>, and long rococo couches and <i>pozzetti</i>, objects meant to be placed against the wall. Bedrooms of rich Venetians were usually sumptuous and grand, with rich damask, velvet, and silk drapery and curtains, and beautifully carved rococo beds with statues of <a href="/wiki/Putti" class="mw-redirect" title="Putti">putti</a>, flowers and angels.<sup id="cite_ref-Miller_2005_p.82_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Miller_2005_p.82-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Venice was especially known for its beautiful <a href="/w/index.php?title=Girandole_mirrors&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Girandole mirrors (page does not exist)">girandole mirrors</a>, which remained among, if not the, finest in Europe. Chandeliers were usually very colourful, using <a href="/wiki/Murano_glass" title="Murano glass">Murano glass</a> to make them look more vibrant and stand out from others, and precious stones and materials from abroad were used, since Venice still held a vast trade empire. Lacquer was very common, and many items of furniture were covered with it, the most noted being <i>lacca povera</i> (poor lacquer), in which allegories and images of social life were painted. Lacquerwork and <a href="/wiki/Chinoiserie" title="Chinoiserie">Chinoiserie</a> were particularly common in bureau cabinets.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Glass">Glass</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Glass">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Venetian_glass" title="Venetian glass">Venetian glass</a> and <a href="/wiki/Murano_glass" title="Murano glass">Murano glass</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Venetian_glass_goblet.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Venetian_glass_goblet.jpg/170px-Venetian_glass_goblet.jpg" width="170" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Venetian_glass_goblet.jpg/255px-Venetian_glass_goblet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c1/Venetian_glass_goblet.jpg 2x" data-file-width="262" data-file-height="315" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Venetian_glass_goblet.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Venetian_glass" title="Venetian glass">Venetian glass</a> <a href="/wiki/Goblet" class="mw-redirect" title="Goblet">goblet</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Venice is known for its ornate glass-work, known as <a href="/wiki/Venetian_glass" title="Venetian glass">Venetian glass</a>. It is world-renowned for being colourful, elaborate, and skilfully made.\n</p><p>Many of the important characteristics of these objects had been developed by the 13th century. Toward the end of that century, the center of the Venetian glass industry moved to <a href="/wiki/Murano" title="Murano">Murano</a>, an offshore island in Venice. The glass made there is known as <a href="/wiki/Murano_glass" title="Murano glass">Murano glass</a>.\n</p><p>Byzantine craftsmen played an important role in the development of Venetian glass, an art form for which the city is well known. When <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> was sacked in the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Crusade" title="Fourth Crusade">Fourth Crusade</a> in 1204, some fleeing artisans came to Venice. This happened again when the <a href="/wiki/Ottomans" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottomans">Ottomans</a> took Constantinople in 1453, supplying Venice with still more glassworkers. By the 16th century, Venetian artisans had gained even greater control over the color and transparency of their glass, and had mastered a variety of decorative techniques.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lampadario_in_vetro_di_Murano_-_Ca%27_Rezzonico,_Venice.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Lampadario_in_vetro_di_Murano_-_Ca%27_Rezzonico%2C_Venice.jpg/170px-Lampadario_in_vetro_di_Murano_-_Ca%27_Rezzonico%2C_Venice.jpg" width="170" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Lampadario_in_vetro_di_Murano_-_Ca%27_Rezzonico%2C_Venice.jpg/255px-Lampadario_in_vetro_di_Murano_-_Ca%27_Rezzonico%2C_Venice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Lampadario_in_vetro_di_Murano_-_Ca%27_Rezzonico%2C_Venice.jpg/340px-Lampadario_in_vetro_di_Murano_-_Ca%27_Rezzonico%2C_Venice.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2078" data-file-height="1798" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lampadario_in_vetro_di_Murano_-_Ca%27_Rezzonico,_Venice.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Murano_glass" title="Murano glass">Murano glass</a> <a href="/wiki/Chandelier" title="Chandelier">chandelier</a> <a href="/wiki/Ca%27_Rezzonico" title="Ca&#39; Rezzonico">Ca\' Rezzonico</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Despite efforts to keep Venetian glassmaking techniques within Venice, they became known elsewhere, and Venetian-style glassware was produced in other Italian cities and other countries of Europe.\n</p><p>Some of the most important brands of glass in the world today are still produced in the historical glass factories on Murano. They are: Venini, Barovier &amp; Toso, <a href="/wiki/Pauly_%26_C._-_Compagnia_Venezia_Murano" class="mw-redirect" title="Pauly &amp; C. - Compagnia Venezia Murano">Pauly</a>, Millevetri, Seguso.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Barovier &amp; Toso is considered one of the 100 <a href="/wiki/List_of_oldest_companies" title="List of oldest companies">oldest companies</a> in the world, formed in 1295.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Cinema.2C_media.2C_and_popular_culture"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema,_media,_and_popular_culture">Cinema, media, and popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Cinema, media, and popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Venice has been the setting or chosen location of numerous films, games, works of fine art and literature (including essays, fiction, non-fiction, and poems), music videos, television shows, and other cultural references.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carnevale_di_Venezia_Masks_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Carnevale_di_Venezia_Masks_2010.jpg/220px-Carnevale_di_Venezia_Masks_2010.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Carnevale_di_Venezia_Masks_2010.jpg/330px-Carnevale_di_Venezia_Masks_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Carnevale_di_Venezia_Masks_2010.jpg/440px-Carnevale_di_Venezia_Masks_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2359" data-file-height="1769" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carnevale_di_Venezia_Masks_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Masks at Carnival of Venice.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:VeniceShopWindow.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/VeniceShopWindow.jpg/220px-VeniceShopWindow.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/VeniceShopWindow.jpg/330px-VeniceShopWindow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/VeniceShopWindow.jpg/440px-VeniceShopWindow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4347" data-file-height="2880" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:VeniceShopWindow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Typical masks worn during the <a href="/wiki/Carnival_of_Venice" title="Carnival of Venice">Carnival of Venice</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Carnival_of_Venice" title="Carnival of Venice">Carnival of Venice</a> is held annually in the city, It lasts for around two weeks and ends on <a href="/wiki/Shrove_Tuesday" title="Shrove Tuesday">Shrove Tuesday</a>. <a href="/wiki/Venetian_mask" class="mw-redirect" title="Venetian mask">Venetian masks</a> are worn.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Venice_Biennale" title="Venice Biennale">Venice Biennale</a> is one of the most important events in the arts calendar. In 1895 an <i>Esposizione biennale artistica nazionale</i> (biennial exhibition of Italian art) was inaugurated.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> The activities of the Biennale were interrupted by the war in September 1942, but resumed in 1948.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Festa_del_Redentore" title="Festa del Redentore">Festa del Redentore</a> is held in mid July. It began as a feast to give thanks for the end of the plague of 1576. A bridge of barges is built connecting Giudecca to the rest of Venice, and fireworks play an important role.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Venice_Film_Festival" title="Venice Film Festival">Venice Film Festival</a> (<span style="font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;" title="in Italian"><a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a></span> <span lang="it"><i>Mostra Internazionale d\'Arte Cinematografica di Venezia</i></span>) is the oldest film festival in the world. <sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Founded by Count <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Volpi_di_Misurata" class="mw-redirect" title="Giuseppe Volpi di Misurata">Giuseppe Volpi di Misurata</a> in 1932 as the <i>Esposizione Internazionale d\'Arte Cinematografica</i>, the festival has since taken place every year in late August or early September on the island of the <a href="/wiki/Lido_di_Venezia" title="Lido di Venezia">Lido</a>. Screenings take place in the historic <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_del_Cinema" class="mw-redirect" title="Palazzo del Cinema">Palazzo del Cinema</a> on the Lungomare Marconi. It is one of the world\'s most prestigious film festivals and is part of the Venice Biennale.\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Carnival_of_Venice" title="Carnival of Venice">Carnival of Venice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venice_Film_Festival" title="Venice Film Festival">Venice Film Festival</a></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="In_films">In films</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: In films">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Examples of films set or at least partially filmed in Venice include:<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Comfort_of_Strangers_(film)" title="The Comfort of Strangers (film)">The Comfort of Strangers</a></i> (1990)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Look_Now" title="Don&#39;t Look Now">Don\'t Look Now</a></i> (1973)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Italian_Job_(2003_film)" title="The Italian Job (2003 film)">The Italian Job</a></i> (2003)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Luchino_Visconti" title="Luchino Visconti">Luchino Visconti</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Death_in_Venice_(film)" title="Death in Venice (film)">Death in Venice</a></i> (1971)<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Three <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="Moonraker (film)">Moonraker</a></i> (1979), and <i><a href="/wiki/Casino_Royale_(2006_film)" title="Casino Royale (2006 film)">Casino Royale</a></i> (2006)</li>\n<li><i><a (1955), starring <a href="/wiki/Katharine_Hepburn" title="Katharine Hepburn">Katharine Hepburn</a></li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Fellini%27s_Casanova" title="Fellini&#39;s Casanova">Fellini\'s Casanova</a></i> (1976)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Woody_Allen" title="Woody Allen">Woody Allen</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Everyone_Says_I_Love_You" title="Everyone Says I Love You">Everyone Says I Love You</a></i> (1996)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Roeg" title="Nicolas Roeg">Nicolas Roeg</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Look_Now" title="Don&#39;t Look Now">Don\'t Look Now</a></i> (1973)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Wings_of_the_Dove_(1997_film)" title="The Wings of the Dove (1997 film)">The Wings of the Dove</a></i> (1997)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Indiana_Jones_and_the_Last_Crusade" title="Indiana Jones and the Last Crusade">Indiana Jones and the Last Crusade</a></i> (1989)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_League_of_Extraordinary_Gentlemen_(film)" title="The League of Extraordinary Gentlemen (film)">The League of Extraordinary Gentlemen</a></i> (2003)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/A_Little_Romance" title="A Little Romance">A Little Romance</a></i> (1979)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Lara_Croft:_Tomb_Raider" title="Lara Croft: Tomb Raider">Lara Croft: Tomb Raider</a></i> (2001)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Talented_Mr._Ripley_(film)" title="The Talented Mr. Ripley (film)">The Talented Mr. Ripley</a></i> (1999)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Dangerous_Beauty" title="Dangerous Beauty">Dangerous Beauty</a></i> (1988), the biography of <a href="/wiki/Veronica_Franco" title="Veronica Franco">Veronica Franco</a></li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Penguins_of_Madagascar" title="Penguins of Madagascar">Penguins of Madagascar</a></i> (2014)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Pok%C3%A9mon_Heroes" title="Pok\xc3\xa9mon Heroes">Pok\xc3\xa9mon Heroes</a></i> (2002), is set inside a city based on Venice, although it is titled differently and features sights not present within its real-world equivalent. (The city is otherwise virtually identical to Venice.)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Blame_It_on_the_Bellboy" title="Blame It on the Bellboy">Blame It on the Bellboy</a></i> (1992)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Inferno_(2016_film)" title="Inferno (2016 film)">Inferno</a></i> (2016)</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Venice" title="Music of Venice">Music of Venice</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Venice_in_media" title="Venice in media">Venice in media</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venetian_polychoral_style" title="Venetian polychoral style">Venetian polychoral style</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Veneto" title="Music of Veneto">Music of Veneto</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Venetian_School_(music)" title="Venetian School (music)">Venetian School (music)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Fenice_Opera_House_from_the_stage.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/La_Fenice_Opera_House_from_the_stage.jpg/220px-La_Fenice_Opera_House_from_the_stage.jpg" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/La_Fenice_Opera_House_from_the_stage.jpg/330px-La_Fenice_Opera_House_from_the_stage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/La_Fenice_Opera_House_from_the_stage.jpg/440px-La_Fenice_Opera_House_from_the_stage.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3724" data-file-height="2960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Fenice_Opera_House_from_the_stage.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/La_Fenice" title="La Fenice">La Fenice</a> operahouse in the city.</div></div></div>\n<p>The city of Venice in Italy has played an important role in the development of the <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Italy" title="Music of Italy">music of Italy</a>. The Venetian state \xe2\x80\x93 i.e., the medieval <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maritime_Republic_of_Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Maritime Republic of Venice (page does not exist)">Maritime Republic of Venice</a> \xe2\x80\x93 was often popularly called the "Republic of Music", and an anonymous Frenchman of the 17th century is said to have remarked that "In every home, someone is playing a musical instrument or singing. There is music everywhere."<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the 16th century, Venice became one of the most important musical centers of Europe, marked by a characteristic style of composition (the <a href="/wiki/Venetian_School_(music)" title="Venetian School (music)">Venetian school</a>) and the development of the <a href="/wiki/Venetian_polychoral_style" title="Venetian polychoral style">Venetian polychoral style</a> under composers such as <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Willaert" title="Adrian Willaert">Adrian Willaert</a>, who worked at <a href="/wiki/San_Marco_di_Venezia" class="mw-redirect" title="San Marco di Venezia">St Mark\'s Basilica</a>. Venice was the early center of music printing; <a href="/wiki/Ottaviano_Petrucci" title="Ottaviano Petrucci">Ottaviano Petrucci</a> began publishing music almost as soon as this technology was available, and his publishing enterprise helped to attract composers from all over Europe, especially from France and <a href="/wiki/Flanders" title="Flanders">Flanders</a>. By the end of the century, Venice was known for the splendor of its music, as exemplified in the "colossal style" of <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Gabrieli" title="Andrea Gabrieli">Andrea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Gabrieli" title="Giovanni Gabrieli">Giovanni Gabrieli</a>, which used multiple choruses and instrumental groups. Venice was also the home of many noted composers during the <a href="/wiki/Baroque_music" title="Baroque music">baroque period</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Vivaldi" title="Antonio Vivaldi">Antonio Vivaldi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ippolito_Ciera" title="Ippolito Ciera">Ippolito Ciera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Picchi" title="Giovanni Picchi">Giovanni Picchi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Girolamo_Dalla_Casa" title="Girolamo Dalla Casa">Girolamo Dalla Casa</a>, to name but a few.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_orchestra">The orchestra</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: The orchestra">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Venice has many orchestras of music: <a href="/wiki/La_Fenice" title="La Fenice">Orchestra della Fenice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rond%C3%B2_Veneziano" title="Rond\xc3\xb2 Veneziano">Rond\xc3\xb2 Veneziano</a>, Interpreti Veneziani, and <a href="/wiki/Venice_Baroque_Orchestra" title="Venice Baroque Orchestra">Venice Baroque Orchestra</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_music">In popular music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: In popular music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The city has been the setting for music videos of such songs as <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>\'s "<a href="/wiki/Like_a_Virgin_(song)" title="Like a Virgin (song)">Like a Virgin</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Siouxsie_and_the_Banshees" title="Siouxsie and the Banshees">Siouxsie and the Banshees</a>\' "<a href="/wiki/Dear_Prudence#Cover_versions" title="Dear Prudence">Dear Prudence</a>" .\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="In_video_games">In video games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: In video games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The city is the setting for parts of such video games as <i><a href="/wiki/Assassin%27s_Creed_II" title="Assassin&#39;s Creed II">Assassin\'s Creed II</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Tomb_Raider_II" title="Tomb Raider II">Tomb Raider II</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> It has also served as inspiration for the fictional city of <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Altissia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Altissia (page does not exist)">Altissia</a></i>, in <i><a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XV" title="Final Fantasy XV">Final Fantasy XV</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> The city also serves as a setting for <i><a href="/wiki/The_House_of_the_Dead_2" title="The House of the Dead 2">The House of the Dead 2</a></i>. The city appears as the first main level in <i><a href="/wiki/Sly_3:_Honor_Among_Thieves" title="Sly 3: Honor Among Thieves">Sly 3: Honor Among Thieves</a></i>.\n</p><p>Venice was the base theme for Soleanna, one of the hub worlds in <i><a href="/wiki/Sonic_the_Hedgehog_(2006_video_game)" title="Sonic the Hedgehog (2006 video game)">Sonic The Hedgehog</a></i>. One of the nine playable characters, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Sonic_the_Hedgehog_characters#Silver_the_Hedgehog" title="List of Sonic the Hedgehog characters">Silver The Hedgehog</a>, was once a <a href="/wiki/Mink" title="Mink">mink</a> named "Venice" during development. The idea was ultimately scrapped.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Photography">Photography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Photography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Photograph_of_Guardi%27s_Regatta_in_Venice_at_the_Frick_Art_Reference_Library.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Photograph_of_Guardi%27s_Regatta_in_Venice_at_the_Frick_Art_Reference_Library.jpg/220px-Photograph_of_Guardi%27s_Regatta_in_Venice_at_the_Frick_Art_Reference_Library.jpg" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Photograph_of_Guardi%27s_Regatta_in_Venice_at_the_Frick_Art_Reference_Library.jpg/330px-Photograph_of_Guardi%27s_Regatta_in_Venice_at_the_Frick_Art_Reference_Library.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Photograph_of_Guardi%27s_Regatta_in_Venice_at_the_Frick_Art_Reference_Library.jpg/440px-Photograph_of_Guardi%27s_Regatta_in_Venice_at_the_Frick_Art_Reference_Library.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2744" data-file-height="1705" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Photograph_of_Guardi%27s_Regatta_in_Venice_at_the_Frick_Art_Reference_Library.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Photograph of Guardi\'s Regatta in Venice at the Frick Art Reference Library.</div></div></div>\n<p>Its splendid architecture, artworks, landscapes, <a href="/wiki/Gondolas" class="mw-redirect" title="Gondolas">gondolas</a>, the alternance of high and low tides, the reflections of light and colors, and the unusual daily scenes in a city living on water, make of Venice and its islands a paradise for photographers both professionals and amateurs. <a href="/wiki/Fulvio_Roiter" title="Fulvio Roiter">Fulvio Roiter</a> has probably been the pioneer in artistic photography in Venice,<sup id="cite_ref-auto_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> followed by a number of authors whose works are often reproduced on postcards, thus reaching a widest international popular exposure.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Venetian_cuisine" title="Venetian cuisine">Venetian cuisine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Veneto_wine" class="mw-redirect" title="Veneto wine">Veneto wine</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pietro_Longhi_La_cioccolata_del_mattino_The_Morning_Chocolate_1775-1780.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Pietro_Longhi_La_cioccolata_del_mattino_The_Morning_Chocolate_1775-1780.jpg/170px-Pietro_Longhi_La_cioccolata_del_mattino_The_Morning_Chocolate_1775-1780.jpg" width="170" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Pietro_Longhi_La_cioccolata_del_mattino_The_Morning_Chocolate_1775-1780.jpg/255px-Pietro_Longhi_La_cioccolata_del_mattino_The_Morning_Chocolate_1775-1780.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Pietro_Longhi_La_cioccolata_del_mattino_The_Morning_Chocolate_1775-1780.jpg/340px-Pietro_Longhi_La_cioccolata_del_mattino_The_Morning_Chocolate_1775-1780.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2536" data-file-height="3286" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pietro_Longhi_La_cioccolata_del_mattino_The_Morning_Chocolate_1775-1780.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hot chocolate was a fashionable drink in Venice during the 1770s and 1780s.</div></div></div>\n<p>Venetian cuisine is characterized by seafood, but also includes garden products from the islands of the lagoon, rice from the mainland, game, and <a href="/wiki/Polenta" title="Polenta">polenta</a>. Venice is not known for a peculiar cuisine of its own: it combines local traditions with influences stemming from age-old contacts with distant countries.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> These include <i>sarde in sa\xc3\xb3r</i> (sardines marinated to preserve them for long voyages); <i>bacal\xc3\xa0 mantecato</i> (a recipe based on Norwegian <a href="/wiki/Stockfish" title="Stockfish">stockfish</a> and extra-virgin olive oil); <i>bis\xc3\xa0to</i> (marinated eel); <i>risi e bisi</i>, rice, peas and (not smoked) bacon;<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> <i>fegato alla veneziana</i>, Venetian-style veal liver; <i>ris\xc3\xb2to col n\xc3\xa9ro de s\xc3\xa9pe</i> (risotto with cuttlefish, blackened by their ink); <i>cich\xc3\xa9ti</i>, refined and delicious tidbits (akin to <i>tapas</i>); <i>antipasti</i> (appetizers); and <i><a href="/wiki/Prosecco" title="Prosecco">prosecco</a></i>, an effervescent, mildly sweet wine.\n</p><p>In addition, Venice is known for the golden, oval-shaped cookies called <i><a href="/wiki/Baicoli" title="Baicoli">ba\xc3\xaccoli</a></i>, and for other types of sweets, such as: <i>pan del pesca\xc3\xb3r</i> (bread of the fisherman); cookies with almonds and pistachio nuts; cookies with fried Venetian cream, or the <i>bussol\xc3\xa0i</i> (<a href="/wiki/Butter_biscuit" class="mw-redirect" title="Butter biscuit">butter biscuits</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shortbread" title="Shortbread">shortbread</a> made in the shape of a ring or of an "S") from the island of Burano; the <i>gal\xc3\xa0ni</i> or <i>cr\xc3\xb3stoli</i> (<a href="/wiki/Angel_wings" title="Angel wings">angel wings</a>);<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> the <i>fr\xc3\xactole</i> (fried spherical doughnuts); the <i>fregol\xc3\xb2tta</i> (a crumbly cake with almonds); a milk pudding called <i>ros\xc3\xa0da</i>; and cookies called <i>zal\xc3\xa9ti</i>, whose ingredients include yellow maize flour.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The dessert <a href="/wiki/Tiramisu" title="Tiramisu">tiramis\xc3\xb9</a> is generally thought to have been invented in <a href="/wiki/Treviso" title="Treviso">Treviso</a> in the 1970s,<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> and is popular in the <a href="/wiki/Veneto" title="Veneto">Veneto</a> area.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fashion_and_shopping">Fashion and shopping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Fashion and shopping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luxury_shops_and_boutiques_along_the_Rialto.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Luxury_shops_and_boutiques_along_the_Rialto.jpg/170px-Luxury_shops_and_boutiques_along_the_Rialto.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Luxury_shops_and_boutiques_along_the_Rialto.jpg/255px-Luxury_shops_and_boutiques_along_the_Rialto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Luxury_shops_and_boutiques_along_the_Rialto.jpg/340px-Luxury_shops_and_boutiques_along_the_Rialto.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2736" data-file-height="3648" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luxury_shops_and_boutiques_along_the_Rialto.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Luxury shops and boutiques along the <a href="/wiki/Rialto_Bridge" title="Rialto Bridge">Rialto Bridge</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In the 14th century, many young Venetian men began wearing tight-fitting multicoloured hose, the designs on which indicated the Compagnie della Calza ("Trouser Club") to which they belonged. The Venetian Senate passed <a href="/wiki/Sumptuary_law" title="Sumptuary law">sumptuary laws</a>, but these merely resulted in changes in fashion in order to circumvent the law. Dull garments were worn over colourful ones, which then were cut to show the hidden colours resulting in the wide spread of men\'s "slashed" fashions in the 15th century.\n</p><p>Today, Venice is a major fashion and shopping centre, not as important as <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a>, and Rome, but on a par with <a href="/wiki/Verona" title="Verona">Verona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turin" title="Turin">Turin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vicenza" title="Vicenza">Vicenza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Naples</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a>. <a href="/wiki/Roberta_di_Camerino" class="mw-redirect" title="Roberta di Camerino">Roberta di Camerino</a> is the only major <a href="/wiki/Italian_fashion" title="Italian fashion">Italian fashion</a> brand to be based in Venice.<sup id="cite_ref-josh_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-josh-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Founded in 1945, it is renowned for its innovative handbags featuring hardware<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2015)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> by Venetian artisans and often covered in locally woven velvet, and has been credited with creating the concept of the easily recognisable <a href="/wiki/It_bag" class="mw-redirect" title="It bag">status bag</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-josh_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-josh-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Many of the fashion boutiques and jewelry shops in the city are located on or near the <a href="/wiki/Rialto_Bridge" title="Rialto Bridge">Rialto Bridge</a> and in the <a href="/wiki/Piazza_San_Marco" title="Piazza San Marco">Piazza San Marco</a>. There are <a href="/wiki/Louis_Vuitton" title="Louis Vuitton">Louis Vuitton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ermenegildo_Zegna" title="Ermenegildo Zegna">Ermenegildo Zegna</a> flagship stores in the city. If shopping for venetian and Italian food specialties and wine you can head to Mascari or Casa del Parmigiano near Rialto and <a href="/w/index.php?title=I_Tre_Mercanti&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="I Tre Mercanti (page does not exist)">I Tre Mercanti</a> flagship store near <a href="/wiki/Piazza_San_Marco" title="Piazza San Marco">Piazza San Marco</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div
