message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Others closely associated with the city include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Pietro_Cesare_Alberti" title="Pietro Cesare Alberti">Pietro Cesare Alberti</a>  (1608\xe2\x80\x931655), considered the first Italian \xe2\x80\x93 American, arriving in New Amsterdam in 1635.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tomaso_Albinoni" title="Tomaso Albinoni">Tomaso Albinoni</a> (8 June 1671 \xe2\x80\x93 17 January 1751), a <a href="/wiki/Baroque_music" title="Baroque music">baroque</a> composer.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Claudio_Ambrosini" title="Claudio Ambrosini">Claudio Ambrosini</a> (9 April 1948), composer and conductor.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pietro_Bembo" title="Pietro Bembo">Pietro Bembo</a> (20 May 1470 \xe2\x80\x93 18 January 1547), <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Cardinal" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic Cardinal">cardinal</a> and scholar.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Bellini" title="Giovanni Bellini">Giovanni Bellini</a> (c. 1430\xe2\x80\x931516), Renaissance painter, probably the best known of the Bellini family of painters.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Francesco_Borgato" title="Francesco Borgato">Francesco Borgato</a> (5 September 1990, Venice), Italian recording artist and dancer.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Marco_Antonio_Bragadin" title="Marco Antonio Bragadin">Marco Antonio Bragadin</a> (d.1571), general, flayed alive by the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Turks</a> after a fierce resistance during the siege of <a href="/wiki/Famagusta" title="Famagusta">Famagusta</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Cabot_(explorer)" title="Sebastian Cabot (explorer)">Sebastian Cabot</a> (c. 1484\xe2\x80\x931557, or soon after), <a href="/wiki/List_of_explorers" title="List of explorers">explorer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rosalba_Carriera" title="Rosalba Carriera">Rosalba Carriera</a> (7 October 1675 \xe2\x80\x93 15 April 1757), known for her pastel works.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Canaletto" title="Canaletto">Canaletto</a> (28 October 1697 \xe2\x80\x93 19 April 1768), known for his landscapes or <i><a href="/wiki/Veduta" title="Veduta">vedute</a></i> of Venice, but not only.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Giacomo_Casanova" title="Giacomo Casanova">Giacomo Casanova</a> (1725\xe2\x80\x931798 in <a href="/wiki/Duchcov" title="Duchcov">Dux</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a>, (now <a href="/wiki/Duchcov" title="Duchcov">Duchcov</a>, Czech Republic)), a Venetian adventurer, writer and <a href="/wiki/Womanizing" class="mw-redirect" title="Womanizing">womanizer</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Francesco_Cavalli" title="Francesco Cavalli">Francesco Cavalli</a> (14 February 1602 \xe2\x80\x93 14 January 1676), a <a href="/wiki/Baroque_music" title="Baroque music">baroque</a> composer.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Da_Ponte" title="Lorenzo Da Ponte">Lorenzo Da Ponte</a> (1749\xe2\x80\x931838), opera librettist and poet, wrote the librettos for 28 operas by 11 composers, including <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Enrico_Dandolo" title="Enrico Dandolo">Enrico Dandolo</a> (<i>c</i>. 1107, 1205), <a href="/wiki/Doge_of_Venice" title="Doge of Venice">Doge of Venice</a> from 1192 to his death, played a direct role in the <a href="/wiki/Sack_of_Constantinople" class="mw-redirect" title="Sack of Constantinople">Sack of Constantinople</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Crusade" title="Fourth Crusade">Fourth Crusade</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Vincenzo_Dandolo" title="Vincenzo Dandolo">Vincenzo Dandolo</a> (1758\xe2\x80\x931819), chemist, agronomist and politician of the <a href="/wiki/Enlightenment_Era" class="mw-redirect" title="Enlightenment Era">Enlightenment Era</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ludovico_de_Luigi" title="Ludovico de Luigi">Ludovico de Luigi</a> (November 1933), Venetian Surrealistic artist.</li>\n<li>Pellegrino Ernetti, Catholic priest and exorcist.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dominic_DeNucci" title="Dominic DeNucci">Dominic DeNucci</a>, (1932\xe2\x80\x93) Professional wrestler</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Veronica_Franco" title="Veronica Franco">Veronica Franco</a> (1546\xe2\x80\x931591), poet and courtesan during the Renaissance.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Andrea_Gabrieli" title="Andrea Gabrieli">Andrea Gabrieli</a> (c. 1510\xe2\x80\x931586), Italian composer and organist at St Mark\'s Basilica.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Gabrieli" title="Giovanni Gabrieli">Giovanni Gabrieli</a> (1554/1557\xe2\x80\x931612), composer and organist at St Mark\'s Basilica.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Carlo_Goldoni" title="Carlo Goldoni">Carlo Goldoni</a> (25 February 1707 \xe2\x80\x93 6 February 1793). Along with <a href="/wiki/Pirandello" class="mw-redirect" title="Pirandello">Pirandello</a>, Goldoni is probably the most notable name in Italian theatre, in his country and abroad.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Carlo_Gozzi" title="Carlo Gozzi">Carlo Gozzi</a> (13 December 1720 \xe2\x80\x93 4 April 1806), dramatist of the 18th century.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pietro_Guarneri" title="Pietro Guarneri">Pietro Guarneri</a> (14 April 1695 \xe2\x80\x93 7 April 1762), left Cremona in 1718, settled in Venice. "Peter of Venice" from the family of great luthiers.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Baldassare_Longhena" title="Baldassare Longhena">Baldassare Longhena</a> (1598\xe2\x80\x9318 February 1682), one of the greatest exponents of Baroque architecture.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Lotto" title="Lorenzo Lotto">Lorenzo Lotto</a> (c. 1480\xe2\x80\x93Loreto, 1556), painter, draughtsman, and illustrator, traditionally placed in the <a href="/wiki/Venetian_School_(art)" class="mw-redirect" title="Venetian School (art)">Venetian school</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bruno_Maderna" title="Bruno Maderna">Bruno Maderna</a> (21 April 1920 \xe2\x80\x93 13 November 1973), an Italian-German orchestra director and 20th-century music composer.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Aldus_Manutius" title="Aldus Manutius">Aldus Manutius</a> (1449\xe2\x80\x931515), one of the most important printers in history.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Leon_Modena" class="mw-redirect" title="Leon Modena">Leon Modena</a> (1571\xe2\x80\x931648) preacher, author, poet, active in the Venetian ghetto and beyond.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Claudio_Monteverdi" title="Claudio Monteverdi">Claudio Monteverdi</a> (1567\xe2\x80\x931643), composer, opera pioneer, and director of music at <a href="/wiki/San_Marco" title="San Marco">San Marco</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Luigi_Nono_(composer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Luigi Nono (composer)">Luigi Nono</a> (29 January 1924 \xe2\x80\x93 8 May 1990), a leading composer of instrumental and electronic music.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Pardo_(rabbi)" title="Joseph Pardo (rabbi)">Joseph Pardo</a> (c. 1561\xe2\x80\x931619), rabbi and merchant.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Elena_Lucrezia_Cornaro_Piscopia" class="mw-redirect" title="Elena Lucrezia Cornaro Piscopia">Elena Lucrezia Cornaro Piscopia</a> (5 June 1646 \xe2\x80\x93 26 July 1684), the first woman in the world to receive a doctorate degree.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">Marco Polo</a> (c. 1254\xe2\x80\x938 January 1324), trader and <a href="/wiki/Exploration" title="Exploration">explorer</a>, one of the first Westerners to travel the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> to China. While a prisoner in Genoa, he dictated in the tale of his travels known as <i>Il Milione</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Travels_of_Marco_Polo" title="The Travels of Marco Polo">The Travels of Marco Polo</a></i>).</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Virgilio_Ranzato" title="Virgilio Ranzato">Virgilio Ranzato</a> (7 May 1883 \xe2\x80\x93 20 April 1937), composer.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Rolfe" title="Frederick Rolfe">Frederick Rolfe</a> (22 July 1860 \xe2\x80\x93 25 October 1913), English author of the Venetian novel <i>The Desire and Pursuit of the Whole</i>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Carlo_Scarpa" title="Carlo Scarpa">Carlo Scarpa</a> (2 June 1906 \xe2\x80\x93 1978, <a href="/wiki/Sendai,_Miyagi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sendai, Miyagi">Sendai, Japan</a>), an architect with a profound understanding of materials.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Romano_Scarpa" title="Romano Scarpa">Romano Scarpa</a> (27 September 1927, Venice\xe2\x80\x9323 April 2005, M\xc3\xa1laga), was one of the most noted Italian creators of Disney comics.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Sinopoli" title="Giuseppe Sinopoli">Giuseppe Sinopoli</a> (2 November 1946 \xe2\x80\x93 20 April 2001), conductor and composer.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Tiepolo" title="Giovanni Battista Tiepolo">Giovanni Battista Tiepolo</a> (5 March 1696 \xe2\x80\x93 27 March 1770), the last "Grand Manner" fresco painter from the Venetian Republic.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tintoretto" title="Tintoretto">Tintoretto</a> (1518\xe2\x80\x9331 May 1594), probably the last great painter of Italian Renaissance.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Titian" title="Titian">Titian</a> (<i>c</i>. 1488\xe2\x80\x9390\xe2\x80\x9327 August 1576), leader of the 16th-century Venetian school of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Renaissance" title="Italian Renaissance">Italian Renaissance</a> (he was born in <a href="/wiki/Cadore" title="Cadore">Pieve di Cadore</a>).</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Elisabetta_Camin%C3%A8r_Turra" title="Elisabetta Camin\xc3\xa8r Turra">Elisabetta Camin\xc3\xa8r Turra</a> (1751\xe2\x80\x931796), writer.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Emilio_Vedova" title="Emilio Vedova">Emilio Vedova</a> (9 August 1919 \xe2\x80\x93 25 October 2006), one of the most important modern painters of Italy.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sebastiano_Venier" title="Sebastiano Venier">Sebastiano Venier</a>, (c. 1496\xe2\x80\x933 March 1578), <a href="/wiki/Doge_of_Venice" title="Doge of Venice">Doge of Venice</a> from 11 June 1577 to 1578.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Antonio_Vivaldi" title="Antonio Vivaldi">Antonio Vivaldi</a> (4 March 1678\xe2\x80\x9328 July (or 27), 1741, <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>), composer and violinist of the Baroque Era.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Domenico_Montagnana" title="Domenico Montagnana">Domenico Montagnana</a>, (24 June 1686 \xe2\x80\x93 6 March 1750) was an Italian master <a href="/wiki/Luthier" title="Luthier">luthier</a>. He is regarded as one of the world\'s finest <a href="/wiki/Violin" title="Violin">violin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cello" title="Cello">cello</a> makers of his time.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The City of Venice and the Central Association of Cities and Communities of Greece (KEDKE) established, in January 2000, in pursuance of the EC Regulations n. 2137/85, the European Economic Interest Grouping (E.E.I.G.) <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">Marco Polo</a> System to promote and realise European projects within transnational cultural and tourist field, particularly referred to the artistic and architectural heritage preservation and safeguard.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_and_sister_cities">Twin towns and sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Twin towns and sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Italy" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Italy">List of twin towns and sister cities in Italy</a></div>\n<p>Venice is <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twinned</a> with:\n</p>\n<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia"><img alt="Armenia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Flag_of_Armenia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Armenia.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Flag_of_Armenia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Armenia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Flag_of_Armenia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Armenia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a>, Armenia, since 2011<sup id="cite_ref-Yerevan_twinnings_2_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yerevan_twinnings_2-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia"><img alt="Croatia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Croatia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Croatia.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Croatia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Croatia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Croatia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Croatia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Dubrovnik" title="Dubrovnik">Dubrovnik</a>, Croatia, since 2012<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n\n<p>In 2013, Venice ended the sister city relationship with St. Petersburg in opposition to laws Russia had passed against homosexuals and those who support gay rights.<sup id="cite_ref-Venice_Russia_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Venice_Russia-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cooperation_agreements">Cooperation agreements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Venice&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Cooperation agreements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Venice has cooperation agreements with the Greek city of <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a>, the German city of <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a>, signed on 25 September 1999, and the Turkish city of <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, signed on 4 March 1993, within the framework of the 1991 Istanbul Declaration. It is also a Science and Technology Partnership City with <a href="/wiki/Qingdao" title="Qingdao">Qingdao</a>, China.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Italy" title="List of islands of Italy">List of islands of Italy</a></li>\n<li><a of the East</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_Italy" title="Outline of Italy">Outline of Italy</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Republic of Venice</a></li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Su_e_zo_per_i_ponti" title="Su e zo per i ponti">Su e zo per i ponti</a></i></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Veneti" title="Adriatic Veneti">Veneti</a> and <a La cucina veneziana</i>, Milano, Franco Angeli, 2008, p. 63</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-132"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-132">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In other areas of Italy similar sweets are known by many other names, e.g. <i>c\xc3\xa9nci</i> (rags) (Florence), <i>frappe</i> (flounces) (Rome), <i>bug\xc3\xace</i> (lies) (Turin, Genoa, etc.), <i>chi\xc3\xa0cchiere</i> (chatter) (Milan and many other places in northern, central and southern Italy). The most important study of the life of Renaissance nuns, with much on aristocratic family networks and the life of women more generally.</li>\n<li>Madden, Thomas F. <i>Enrico Dandolo and the Rise of Venice</i> Johns Hopkins University Press. Probably the best book in English on medieval Venice.</li>\n<li>Martin, John Jeffries and Dennis Romano (eds). <i>Venice Reconsidered. The History and Civilization of an Italian City-State, 1297\xe2\x80\x931797.</i> (2002) <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University_Press" title="Johns Hopkins University Press">Johns Hopkins University Press</a>. The most recent collection on essays, many by prominent scholars, on Venice.</li>\n<li>Muir, Edward (1981). <i>Civic Ritual in Renaissance Venice.</i> Princeton UP. The classic of Venetian cultural studies, highly sophisticated.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gerald_J._Oppenheimer" title="Gerald J. Oppenheimer">Oppenheimer, Gerald J.</a> (2010). <i>Venetian</i> Palazzi <i>and</i> Case: <i>A Guide to the Literature.</i> University of Washington, Seattle. Geschichte einer Seerepublik.</i> Stuttgart: Kohlhammer. In German, but the most recent top-level brief history of Venice.</li>\n<li><cite class="citation book">Miller, Judith (2005). <i>Furniture: world styles from classical to contemporary</i>.
